The **Marvel Cinematic Universe** (**MCU**) is an American [media franchise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_franchise "Media franchise") and [shared universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shared_universe "Shared universe") centered on [a series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films "List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films") of [superhero films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superhero_film "Superhero film") produced by [Marvel Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Studios "Marvel Studios"). The films are based on characters from [American comic books](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_comic_book "American comic book") published by [Marvel Comics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Comics "Marvel Comics"). The franchise also includes [several television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_television_series "List of Marvel Cinematic Universe television series"), short films, digital series, and literature. The shared universe, much like the original [Marvel Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Universe "Marvel Universe") in comic books, was established by [crossing over](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crossover_(fiction) "Crossover (fiction)") common plot elements, settings, cast, and characters.

Marvel Studios releases its films in groups called "Phases", with the first three phases collectively known as "The Infinity Saga" and the following three phases as "The Multiverse Saga". The first MCU film, _[Iron Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron\_Man\_(2008\_film) "Iron Man (2008 film)")_ (2008), began [Phase One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_One "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One"), which culminated in the 2012 crossover film _[The Avengers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Avengers\_(2012\_film) "The Avengers (2012 film)")_. [Phase Two](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Two "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Two") began with _[Iron Man 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron\_Man\_3 "Iron Man 3")_ (2013) and concluded with _[Ant-Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant-Man\_(film) "Ant-Man (film)")_ (2015), while [Phase Three](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Three "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Three") began with _[Captain America: Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_America:\_Civil\_War "Captain America: Civil War")_ (2016) and concluded with _[Spider-Man: Far From Home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_Far\_From\_Home "Spider-Man: Far From Home")_ (2019). _[Black Widow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black\_Widow\_(2021\_film) "Black Widow (2021 film)")_ (2021) is the first film in [Phase Four](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Four "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Four"), which concluded with _[Black Panther: Wakanda Forever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black\_Panther:\_Wakanda\_Forever "Black Panther: Wakanda Forever")_ (2022), while [Phase Five](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Five "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Five") began with _[Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant-Man\_and\_the\_Wasp:\_Quantumania "Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania")_ (2023) and concluded with _[Thunderbolts*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thunderbolts* "Thunderbolts*")_ (2025). [Phase Six](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Six "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Six") began with _[The Fantastic Four: First Steps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Fantastic\_Four:\_First\_Steps "The Fantastic Four: First Steps")_ (2025) and will conclude with _[Avengers: Secret Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Secret\_Wars "Avengers: Secret Wars")_ (2027).

[Marvel Television](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Television "Marvel Television") expanded the universe to network television with _[Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agents\_of\_S.H.I.E.L.D. "Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.")_ on [ABC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company "American Broadcasting Company") in 2013 before further expanding to [streaming television](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Streaming_television "Streaming television") on [Netflix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netflix "Netflix") and [Hulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulu "Hulu") and to [cable television](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cable_television "Cable television") on [Freeform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freeform_(TV_channel) "Freeform (TV channel)"). They also produced the digital series _[Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.: Slingshot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agents\_of\_S.H.I.E.L.D.:\_Slingshot "Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.: Slingshot")_ (2016). Marvel Studios began producing its own television series for the streaming service [Disney+](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+"), starting with _[WandaVision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WandaVision "WandaVision")_ in 2021, marking the beginning of Phase Four. That phase also saw the studio expand to television specials, known as [Marvel Studios Special Presentations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Studios_Special_Presentations "Marvel Studios Special Presentations"), starting with _[Werewolf by Night](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Werewolf\_by\_Night\_(TV\_special) "Werewolf by Night (TV special)")_ (2022). The MCU includes [various tie-in comics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_tie-in_comics "Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics") published by Marvel Comics, a series of direct-to-video short films called [Marvel One-Shots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_One-Shots "Marvel One-Shots") from 2011 to 2014, and [viral marketing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_marketing "Viral marketing") campaigns for some films featuring the faux news programs _[WHIH Newsfront](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WHIH\_Newsfront "WHIH Newsfront")_ (2015–16) and _[The Daily Bugle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Daily\_Bugle\_(web\_series) "The Daily Bugle (web series)")_ (2019–2022).

The franchise has been commercially successful, becoming one of the [highest-grossing media franchises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_media_franchises "List of highest-grossing media franchises") of all time, and it has received generally positive reviews from critics. However, many of the Multiverse Saga projects performed below expectations and struggled compared to those of the Infinity Saga. The studio has attributed this to the increased amount of content produced after the 2019 film _[Avengers: Endgame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Endgame "Avengers: Endgame")_, and as of 2024, began decreasing its content output. The MCU has inspired other film and television studios to attempt similar shared universes and has also inspired several themed attractions, an art exhibit, television specials, literary material, multiple tie-in video games, and commercials.

Development
-----------

### Marvel Studios films and series

#### The Infinity Saga films

By 2005, [Marvel Entertainment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment "Marvel Entertainment") was planning to produce its own films independently and distribute them through [Paramount Pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paramount_Pictures "Paramount Pictures").[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Variety2005-1) Previously, Marvel had [co-produced](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Co-production_(filmmaking) "Co-production (filmmaking)")[several superhero films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Studios#Formation_of_Marvel_Studios_and_licensing_films_(1996%E2%80%932004) "Marvel Studios") based on [Marvel Comics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Comics "Marvel Comics") with [Columbia Pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbia_Pictures "Columbia Pictures"), [New Line Cinema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Line_Cinema "New Line Cinema"), [20th Century Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/20th_Century_Fox "20th Century Fox"), and others.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Variety2006-2) Marvel made relatively little profit from these licensing deals and wanted to get more money out of its films while maintaining artistic control of the projects and distribution.[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-June2007NYTimes-3)[Avi Arad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avi_Arad "Avi Arad"), head of Marvel Entertainment's film division known as [Marvel Films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Films "Marvel Films"), was pleased with director [Sam Raimi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sam_Raimi "Sam Raimi")'s [_Spider-Man_ film trilogy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man_(2002_film_series) "Spider-Man (2002 film series)") (2002–2007) at [Sony Pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sony_Pictures "Sony Pictures") and Columbia but was less enthused with some of the other films. Arad decided to form [Marvel Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Studios "Marvel Studios"), Hollywood's first major [independent film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Independent_film "Independent film") studio since [DreamWorks Pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DreamWorks_Pictures "DreamWorks Pictures") was founded in 1994. [Kevin Feige](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Feige "Kevin Feige"), Arad's second-in-command,[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BloombergPg3-4) realized that unlike [Spider-Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man "Spider-Man"), [Blade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blade_(character) "Blade (character)"), and the [X-Men](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-Men "X-Men") which were respectively licensed to Sony, New Line, and Fox, Marvel owned the rights to the [Avengers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers_(comics) "Avengers (comics)") team. Feige, a self-described "fanboy", envisioned combining these characters in a [shared universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shared_universe "Shared universe") similar to the one created by [Stan Lee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stan_Lee "Stan Lee") and [Jack Kirby](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jack_Kirby "Jack Kirby") for Marvel Comics in the 1960s.[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BostonApril2012-5)

> "It's never been done before and that's kind of the spirit everybody's taking it in. The other filmmakers aren't used to getting actors from other movies that other filmmakers have cast, certain plot lines that are connected or certain locations that are connected, but I think... everyone was on board for it and thinks that it's fun. Primarily because we've always remained consistent saying that the movie that we are making comes first. All of the connective tissue, all of that stuff is fun and is going to be very important if you want it to be. If the fans want to look further and find connections, then they're there. There are a few big ones obviously, that hopefully the mainstream audience will [be] able to follow as well. But... the reason that all the filmmakers are on board is that their movies need to stand on their own. They need to have a fresh vision, a unique tone, and the fact that they can interconnect if you want to follow those breadcrumbs is a bonus."

—Marvel Studios president Kevin Feige on constructing a shared film universe[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeQuote-6)

To raise capital, the studio secured funding from a seven-year, $525 million revolving credit facility with [Merrill Lynch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merrill_Lynch "Merrill Lynch").[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-June2007NYTimes-3) Marvel planned to release individual films for their main characters and then merge them in a [crossover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crossover_(fiction) "Crossover (fiction)") film;[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CinematicalCrossover-7) Arad, who resigned in 2006, doubted this strategy would work. He insisted that his reputation helped secure the initial financing.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BloombergPg3-4)[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DailyMarsMay2014-8) In 2007, Feige was named studio chief. To preserve its artistic integrity, Marvel Studios formed a creative committee of six people familiar with its comic book lore: Feige, Marvel Studios co-president [Louis D'Esposito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_D%27Esposito "Louis D'Esposito"), Marvel Comics' president of publishing [Dan Buckley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dan_Buckley "Dan Buckley"), Marvel Entertainment's chief creative officer [Joe Quesada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Quesada "Joe Quesada"), comic book writer [Brian Michael Bendis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Michael_Bendis "Brian Michael Bendis"), and Marvel Entertainment president [Alan Fine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Fine_(executive) "Alan Fine (executive)"), who oversaw the committee.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BloombergPg3-4) Feige initially referred to the shared narrative [continuity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuity_(fiction) "Continuity (fiction)") of the films as the "Marvel Cinema Universe",[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeCinemaUniverse-9) but later used the term "Marvel Cinematic Universe".[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeCinematicUniverse-10) Since the franchise expanded to other media, some have used this phrase to only refer to the feature films.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MCUFilmsOnly-11)

The MCU films are released in groups called "Phases", beginning with [Phase One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_One "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One") and [Phase Two](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Two "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Two").[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DailyDotPhases-12)[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DigitalSpyPhases-13) In December 2009, [the Walt Disney Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company "The Walt Disney Company") purchased Marvel Entertainment for $4 billion. Disney said future Marvel Studios films would be distributed by [its own studio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures "Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures") once the prior deal with Paramount expired.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DisneyMarvel-14)[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DisneyMarvel2-15) The films of [Phase Three](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Three "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Three") were announced at a special press event in October 2014.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Oct2014Event-16) By September 2015, Marvel Studios was integrated into [Walt Disney Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division) "Walt Disney Studios (division)"). Feige was reporting to Walt Disney Studios chairman [Alan F. Horn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_F._Horn "Alan F. Horn") instead of Marvel Entertainment CEO [Isaac Perlmutter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Perlmutter "Isaac Perlmutter"),[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MarvelDisneyAug2015-17) and the creative committee began having only "nominal" input on the films. They continued to consult on [Marvel Television](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Television "Marvel Television") productions, which remained under Perlmutter's control.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CreativeCommitteeEnd-18)[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CreativeCommittee2-19) All key film decisions moving forward were to be made by Feige, D'Esposito, and executive vice president [Victoria Alonso](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victoria_Alonso "Victoria Alonso").[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CreativeCommitteeEnd-18) The studio went on to establish the [Marvel Studios Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Studios_Parliament "Marvel Studios Parliament"), a "brain trust" of long-time executives at the company who help to elevate each other's projects where possible.[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Parliament-20) In November 2017, Feige said _[Avengers: Endgame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Endgame "Avengers: Endgame")_ (2019) would provide a definitive conclusion to the films thus far and begin a new period for the franchise.[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VanityFairNov2017-21) He later said Phase Three would conclude "[The Infinity Saga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Infinity_Saga "The Infinity Saga")".[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FFHInfinitySaga-22)

#### The Multiverse Saga films and series

Disney reportedly began developing a Marvel-based television series for its new streaming service [Disney+](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+") by November 2017.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DisneyStreaming-23) In July 2018, Feige said discussions had begun with Disney regarding any potential involvement Marvel Studios could have with the streaming service, which he felt was important for the wider company.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeStreamingServiceJul2018-24) In September 2018, Marvel Studios was reported to be developing several limited series centered on "second-tier" characters from the MCU films who had not and were unlikely to headline their own films. Each series was expected to be six to eight episodes and would be produced by Marvel Studios rather than Marvel Television, with Feige taking a "hands-on role" in each series' development.[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Disney+SeriesSep2018-25) Feige said these series would "tell stories... that we wouldn't be able to tell in a theatrical experience—a longer-form narrative".[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeStreamingTHRNov2018-26) He added that being asked by Disney to create these series "energized everyone creatively" within Marvel Studios, since they "could play in a new medium and throw the rules out the window in terms of structure and format".[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-EWWVNov2020CoverStory-27)[Television specials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television_specials "Television specials") from the studio are marketed as "[Marvel Studios Special Presentations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Studios_Special_Presentations "Marvel Studios Special Presentations")".[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MarvelStudiosSpecialPresentation-28)[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GotGHSMSSP-29)_[The Guardians of the Galaxy Holiday Special](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Guardians\_of\_the\_Galaxy\_Holiday\_Special "The Guardians of the Galaxy Holiday Special")_ (2022), a Special Presentation, was the first project Marvel Studios began planning for Disney+.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GotGHSFirstContent-30)

[![Image 7: Kevin Feige speaking at the 2019 San Diego Comic-Con International](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Kevin_Feige_%2848462887397%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Kevin_Feige_%2848462887397%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kevin_Feige_(48462887397)_(cropped).jpg)

Kevin Feige helped conceive a shared media universe of Marvel properties[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BloombergPg3-4)

In July 2019, Feige announced the [Phase Four](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Four "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Four") slate at [San Diego Comic-Con](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con "San Diego Comic-Con"), consisting of films and, for the first time, television event series on Disney+.[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-THRPhase4SDCC-31) The Phase Four slate includes _[What If...?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/What\_If...%3F\_(TV\_series) "What If...? (TV series)")_, the first animated series from Marvel Studios, and by July 2021 the studio was creating an "animation branch and mini studio",[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AnimationBranch-32) known as [Marvel Studios Animation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Studios_Animation "Marvel Studios Animation"),[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MarvelStudiosAnimationName-33) to focus on more animated content beyond _What If...?_.[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AnimationBranch-32) Alonso said Marvel had around 31 projects in various stages of development by September 2021.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Alonso31Projects-34) In April 2022, Feige said he and Marvel Studios were on a creative retreat to plan and discuss the MCU films for the following 10 years.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeRetreatApr2022-35) That July, Feige announced some of the films and series for [Phase Five](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Five "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Five") and [Phase Six](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Six "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Six") at San Diego Comic-Con, revealing that the second three Phases were collectively known as "[The Multiverse Saga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Multiverse_Saga "The Multiverse Saga")".[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SDCC2022-36) After the "creative experience" of ending Phase Three and "The Infinity Saga" with _[Avengers: Infinity War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Infinity\_War "Avengers: Infinity War")_ (2018) and _Avengers: Endgame_, and the expansion in the number of projects being produced by the studio in a short amount of time, Marvel Studios decided to move away from having an Avengers crossover film at the end of each Phase and instead decided to have a crossover culmination at the end of "The Multiverse Saga" with the planned film _[Avengers: The Kang Dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_The\_Kang\_Dynasty "Avengers: The Kang Dynasty")_ and _[Avengers: Secret Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Secret\_Wars "Avengers: Secret Wars")_ (2027).[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeAvengersPhase6-37) The studio was excited to explore [Kang the Conqueror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kang_the_Conqueror_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Kang the Conqueror (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") as an overarching villain of the Multiverse Saga after [Thanos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thanos_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Thanos (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in the Infinity Saga, because Kang was a different villain in part because he has multiple variants from different timelines within the multiverse.[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeFeb2023-38) The studio did not initially plan to build the next saga around Kang, and made that decision after seeing actor [Jonathan Majors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Majors "Jonathan Majors")'s performance in the [first season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loki_season_1 "Loki season 1") of the Disney+ series _[Loki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loki\_(TV\_series) "Loki (TV series)")_ (2021), as well as [dailies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dailies "Dailies") from the filming of _[Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant-Man\_and\_the\_Wasp:\_Quantumania "Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania")_ (2023).[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-RobinsonKangFocus-39) After Majors was [found guilty of assault and harassment amidst legal issues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Majors#2023_assault "Jonathan Majors") in December 2023, he was fired by Disney and Marvel Studios. At that time, Marvel was internally referring to _The Kang Dynasty_ as _Avengers 5_;[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MajorsFiredTHR-40) by early 2024, Marvel had decided to drop the Kang storyline and began searching for a new antagonist for the saga.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WSJMay2025-41)

Alonso was fired from her role at Marvel Studios in March 2023 for serving as a producer on the [Amazon Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_Studios "Amazon Studios") film _[Argentina, 1985](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argentina,\_1985 "Argentina, 1985")_ (2022), in breach of a 2018 agreement between Alonso and Disney that prohibited her from working for a competing studio. The decision was made by a group that included [Disney Entertainment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disney_Entertainment "Disney Entertainment") co-chairman Alan Bergman and Disney's human resources and legal departments.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AlonsoFiringTHRReason-42)[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AlonsoFired-43) Alonso reportedly did not seek permission to work on the film and was asked by Disney to stop working on it or promoting it. The situation was deemed serious enough that Disney requested a new agreement be signed. The company consistently reminded her of this while she continued to promote the film following its September 2022 premiere, ultimately leading to her firing.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AlonsoFiringTHRReason-42) Alonso's lawyers refuted these claims, saying Disney was aware of, and agreed to, Alonso's work on _Argentina, 1985_ and Alonso had been "silenced [and] was terminated when she refused to do something she believed was reprehensible";[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AlonsoFiringVarietyReason-44) this was reported to be a disagreement with a Disney executive over the censoring of [gay pride elements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_symbols "LGBT symbols") in _Quantumania_ so the film could be released in Kuwait in compliance with [the country's restrictive anti-LGBTQ laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Kuwait "LGBT rights in Kuwait").[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AlonsoFiringDeadlineReason-45)[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AlonsoKuwaitTHR-46) A Disney spokesperson reiterated that Alonso was fired due to "an indisputable breach of contract and a direct violation of company policy" among other factors.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AlonsoFiringVarietyReason-44) Disney and Alonso reached a multi-million dollar compensation settlement in April.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AlonsoSettlement-47)

Disney CEO [Bob Iger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Iger "Bob Iger") said in July 2023 that the company would be reducing the amount of Marvel content created moving forward, admitting that Marvel Studios' expansion into Disney+ series and more films had "diluted focus and attention" after several underachieving films at the box office.[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IgerJul2023-48)[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IgerJul2023Variety-49) He clarified their plans in May 2024, saying Disney would now release two, or at most three, Marvel films and two Marvel series a year. This was a decrease from up to four films and around four series being released in some recent years. The company was reducing output and focusing on quality across all its divisions, but Iger felt the change was especially needed for Marvel.[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IgerContentOutputMay2024-50) Feige and D'Esposito said 2023 had been a particularly difficult year for the studio but they had learned their lesson on trying to make too much content at once. They added that no longer being "on top" of the box office allowed them to be underdogs again, as they had been when starting work on Phase One, and they would be "coming back strong" with the hope of surprising audiences and exceeding expectations.[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeD'EspositoEmpireMay2024-51) Feige expected the studio to begin releasing two films and three series per year after 2025, when they were planning to release three films and six series that had been in development for a long time and were ready to be released.[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeReleaseExpectationOct2024-52) In May 2025, Iger called _Thunderbolts*_ the "first and best example" of Marvel Studios refocusing efforts.[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IgerMay2025-53) In July, Feige said the studio had reduced the budgets of their 2024 and 2025 films to be a third lower than those for 2022 and 2023.[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeConferenceJul2025THR-54)

In 2024, Marvel Studios introduced their "Marvel Animation" and "Marvel Television" banners for their animated and live-action series, respectively. This was done, along with the previously established [Marvel Spotlight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Spotlight_(banner) "Marvel Spotlight (banner)") banner, to help indicate to audiences that they did not have to watch all of the studio's projects to understand the overall story and could choose which storylines and characters under these banners to follow.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WinderbaumBannersMay2024-55) At San Diego Comic-Con 2024, the fifth _Avengers_ film was retitled _[Avengers: Doomsday](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Doomsday "Avengers: Doomsday")_ (2026), with [Robert Downey Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Downey_Jr. "Robert Downey Jr.") cast as the Multiverse Saga's new antagonist [Victor von Doom / Doctor Doom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctor_Doom "Doctor Doom") (after previously portraying the superhero [Tony Stark / Iron Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Stark_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Tony Stark (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in the MCU from 2008 to 2019) for both _Doomsday_ and _Secret Wars_.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SDCC2024Avengers-56) Following several critical and financial failures, the studio began testing its films through test screenings organized by the National Research Group (NRG). The studio previously relied on "friends-and-family" test screenings at [Walt Disney Studios in Burbank, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(Burbank) "Walt Disney Studios (Burbank)"), to help maintain secrecy. Feige said the NRG tests yielded results similar to their own.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeConferenceJul2025Deadline2-57) By July 2025, [Sacha Baron Cohen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacha_Baron_Cohen "Sacha Baron Cohen")'s [Mephisto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mephisto_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Mephisto (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") was being viewed as the next "prominent" villain of the MCU.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CohenMephistoWorkout-58)[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeConferenceJul2025TotalFilm-59)

##### Integration of mutant characters and the X-Men

In December 2017, [Disney agreed to acquire assets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney "Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney") from [21st Century Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/21st_Century_Fox "21st Century Fox"),[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FoxDisneyPressRelease-60) and finalized the transaction on March 19, 2019.[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DisneyFoxDealClose-61) This saw the return of the film rights for [Deadpool](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deadpool "Deadpool"), the X-Men, and the [Fantastic Four](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantastic_Four "Fantastic Four") to Marvel Studios,[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FoxDisneyPressRelease-60) although Feige explained that despite the acquisition being completed in 2019, access and integration of these characters and concepts were unavailable "for a very long time" because of corporate acquisition laws.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DPWEWCoverJun2024-62) Some of the first elements to be integrated into the MCU following the acquisition were the organization [S.W.O.R.D.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S.W.O.R.D._(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "S.W.O.R.D. (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in the Disney+ series _[WandaVision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WandaVision "WandaVision")_ (2021) and the fictional country [Madripoor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madripoor_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Madripoor (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in the series _[The Falcon and the Winter Soldier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Falcon\_and\_the\_Winter\_Soldier "The Falcon and the Winter Soldier")_ (2021).[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FoxElements-63)[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Madripoor-64) Additionally, [Patrick Stewart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrick_Stewart "Patrick Stewart") appeared as Professor [Charles Xavier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Xavier_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Charles Xavier (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in the film _[Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctor\_Strange\_in\_the\_Multiverse\_of\_Madness "Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness")_ (2022), portraying a different version of the character that he previously played in Fox's [_X-Men_ film series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-Men_(film_series) "X-Men (film series)"),[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-StewartMoM-65) while [Kamala Khan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamala_Khan_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Kamala Khan (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") was revealed to have a genetic mutation in _[Ms. Marvel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ms.\_Marvel\_(miniseries) "Ms. Marvel (miniseries)")_,[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MsMarvelMutation-66) with star [Iman Vellani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iman_Vellani "Iman Vellani") confirming that she is the first [mutant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutant_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Mutant (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") (a term related to the X-Men) in the MCU.[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VellaniMutantConfirm-67)[Namor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Namor_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Namor (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") is also revealed to be a mutant in the film _[Black Panther: Wakanda Forever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black\_Panther:\_Wakanda\_Forever "Black Panther: Wakanda Forever")_ (2022), as he is in the comics.[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-EmpireHuerta-68)[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeFeb2023-38)[Kelsey Grammer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelsey_Grammer "Kelsey Grammer") appears as [Dr. Hank McCoy / Beast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beast_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Beast (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in _[The Marvels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Marvels "The Marvels")_ (2023), reprising the role from the _X-Men_ films. The film also introduces the mutant [Binary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Binary (Marvel Cinematic Universe)"), an alternate version of [Maria Rambeau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maria_Rambeau "Maria Rambeau"), portrayed by [Lashana Lynch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lashana_Lynch "Lashana Lynch").[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GrammerMarvels-69)[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GrammerMarvels2-70)

Feige called _[Deadpool & Wolverine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deadpool\_%26\_Wolverine "Deadpool & Wolverine")_ (2024) the true start to Marvel Studios' exploration and use of the Fox characters,[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DPWEWCoverJun2024-62) and said every project after it would be part of the MCU's "Mutant era".[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeMutantEra-71) Some of the films between _Deadpool & Wolverine_ and _Secret Wars_ featured additional X-Men characters, with Feige saying the story of _Secret Wars_ would lead into a "new age of mutants" and the X-Men being introduced to the MCU.[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeNov2024-72)_Doomsday_ sees additional _X-Men_ film series actors reprising their roles, including [Ian McKellen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ian_McKellen "Ian McKellen") as [Erik Lensherr / Magneto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magneto_(film_character) "Magneto (film character)"), [Alan Cumming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Cumming "Alan Cumming") as [Kurt Wagner / Nightcrawler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nightcrawler_(character) "Nightcrawler (character)"), [Rebecca Romijn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebecca_Romijn "Rebecca Romijn") as [Raven Darkhölme / Mystique](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mystique_(film_character) "Mystique (film character)"), and [James Marsden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Marsden "James Marsden") as [Scott Summers / Cyclops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyclops_(Marvel_Comics) "Cyclops (Marvel Comics)"). Stewart and Grammer also reprise their roles in the film.[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DoomsdayXMenCast-73) Feige reportedly has a 10-year plan for the X-Men in the MCU.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WSJMay2025-41)

##### Next saga

In July 2025, Feige said Marvel Studios was "already well into development" on the three phases of their next saga following the conclusion of the Multiverse Saga with _Secret Wars_. He said Phase Seven would be "directly impacted" by the films of Phase Six.[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeConferenceJul2025TotalFilm-59)

### Marvel Television series

[![Image 8](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Jeph_Loeb_San_Diego_Comic_Con_2019.jpg/250px-Jeph_Loeb_San_Diego_Comic_Con_2019.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jeph_Loeb_San_Diego_Comic_Con_2019.jpg)

Jeph Loeb led Marvel Television and served as executive producer of every television series on ABC, Netflix, Hulu, and Freeform

Marvel Television was launched in June 2010 with [Jeph Loeb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeph_Loeb "Jeph Loeb") as head,[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-TVLaunch-74) and had entered into discussions with [ABC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company "American Broadcasting Company") to create a show set in the MCU by July 2012;[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-July2012TVshow-75) the network went on to release _[Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agents\_of\_S.H.I.E.L.D. "Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.")_, _[Agent Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent\_Carter\_(TV\_series) "Agent Carter (TV series)")_,[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AtwellAgentCarterTV-76) and _[Inhumans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inhumans\_(TV\_series) "Inhumans (TV series)")_. The latter was a co-production with [IMAX Corporation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMAX_Corporation "IMAX Corporation").[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-InhumansAnnouncement-77)[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-InhumansAnnouncement2-78)[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-InhumansNoThe-79) In November 2013, Disney was set to provide [Netflix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netflix "Netflix") with the live-action series _[Daredevil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daredevil\_(TV\_series) "Daredevil (TV series)")_, _[Jessica Jones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jessica\_Jones\_(TV\_series) "Jessica Jones (TV series)")_, _[Luke Cage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luke\_Cage\_(TV\_series) "Luke Cage (TV series)")_, and _[Iron Fist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron\_Fist\_(TV\_series) "Iron Fist (TV series)")_, building up to the crossover miniseries _[The Defenders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Defenders\_(miniseries) "The Defenders (miniseries)")_.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DeadlineTVNov2013-80) In April 2016, Netflix ordered _[The Punisher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Punisher\_(TV\_series) "The Punisher (TV series)")_, a spin-off of _Daredevil_.[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PunisherEWApr2016-81) By February 2019, Netflix had canceled all of its Marvel series.[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-JJPunisherCanceled-82) In April 2016, the Disney-owned [cable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cable_television "Cable television") network [Freeform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freeform_(TV_channel) "Freeform (TV channel)") announced _[Cloak & Dagger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloak\_%26\_Dagger\_(TV\_series) "Cloak & Dagger (TV series)")_.[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CloakandDaggerApr2016-83) In May 2017, Marvel announced that _[Runaways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Runaways\_(TV\_series) "Runaways (TV series)")_ had received a series order from [Hulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulu "Hulu").[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-RunawaysSeriesOrder-84) In May 2019, Marvel announced that _[Helstrom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helstrom\_(TV\_series) "Helstrom (TV series)")_ had been greenlit for Hulu.[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-HuluGRH-85)

In October 2019, further corporate restructuring saw Feige named Chief Creative Officer of Marvel Entertainment, with Marvel Television becoming part of Marvel Studios and executives of Marvel Television reporting to Feige.[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Oct2019Restructure-86) In December 2019, Marvel Television was folded into Marvel Studios, with Marvel Studios taking over production of the remaining series and no further series expected to be developed by Marvel Television.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MarvelTVFolded-87) In January 2021, Feige said "never say never" to potentially reviving the Netflix series, but noted that Marvel Studios was focused on their new Disney+ series.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DeadlineFeigeJan2021-88) In May 2022, Marvel Studios was revealed to be developing a new _Daredevil_ series for Disney+,[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DaredevilCormanOrd-89) which was announced in July as _[Daredevil: Born Again](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daredevil:\_Born\_Again "Daredevil: Born Again")_.[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SDCC2022-36)

### Expansion to other media

In 2008, the first [comic book to tie into the MCU](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_tie-in_comics "Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics") was released.[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FirstComic-90) Quesada explained that these comics would be set within the continuity of the films, but were not intended to be direct adaptations. Rather, they would explore "something that happened off screen" or flesh out something briefly mentioned. Feige was involved with the creation of the comics, with the film's screenwriters sometimes as well.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-QuesadaComicBooks-91) Marvel Comics worked with [Brad Winderbaum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brad_Winderbaum "Brad Winderbaum"), [Jeremy Latcham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremy_Latcham "Jeremy Latcham"), and Will Corona Pilgrim at Marvel Studios to decide which concepts would be carried over from the Marvel Comics Universe to the Marvel Cinematic Universe, what to show in the tie-in comics, and what to leave for the films.[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IM2comics-92) Marvel later clarified which of the tie-in comics are considered canonical MCU stories, with the rest being merely inspired by the MCU "where we get to show off all the characters from the film in costume and in comic form".[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PilgrimCanon2015-93)

In August 2011, Marvel announced a series of [direct-to-video](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct-to-video "Direct-to-video")[short films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short_film "Short film") called [Marvel One-Shots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_One-Shots "Marvel One-Shots").[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-OneShotsAnnouncement-94) The name was derived from the label used by Marvel Comics for their [one-shot comics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-shot_(comics) "One-shot (comics)").[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AssemblingAUniverse-95) Winderbaum said the shorts were "a fun way to experiment with new characters and ideas" and to expand the MCU.[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-OneShotsAnnouncement-94) Each short was designed to be a self-contained story that provided more backstory for characters or events introduced in the films.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ShortsDescription-96)

In March 2015, Marvel's vice president of animation development and production, [Cort Lane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cort_Lane "Cort Lane"), said animated tie-ins to the MCU were "in the works".[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LaneECCC2015-97) That July, Marvel Studios partnered with [Google](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google "Google") to produce the faux news program _[WHIH Newsfront with Christine Everhart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WHIH\_Newsfront "WHIH Newsfront")_, a series of in-universe [YouTube](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube "YouTube") videos serving as the center of a [viral marketing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_marketing "Viral marketing") campaign to promote the films and universe.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WHIHPromo-98) In December 2016, a six-part web series, _[Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.: Slingshot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agents\_of\_S.H.I.E.L.D.:\_Slingshot "Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.: Slingshot")_, debuted on [ABC.com](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ABC.com "ABC.com"). It follows [Elena "Yo-Yo" Rodriguez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elena_Rodriguez "Elena Rodriguez") on a secret mission, shortly before the start of _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._'s[fourth season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agents_of_S.H.I.E.L.D._season_4 "Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D. season 4"), with [Natalia Cordova-Buckley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natalia_Cordova-Buckley "Natalia Cordova-Buckley") reprising her role from the series.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Slingshot-99) In September 2019, Sony created a real version of the fictional _[The Daily Bugle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Daily\_Bugle\_(web\_series) "The Daily Bugle (web series)")_ website as part of a viral marketing campaign to promote the home media release of _[Spider-Man: Far From Home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_Far\_From\_Home "Spider-Man: Far From Home")_ (2019). Inspired by real-world "conspiracy-pushing" websites such as [Alex Jones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Jones "Alex Jones")'s _[InfoWars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/InfoWars "InfoWars")_, the website features [J. K. Simmons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._K._Simmons "J. K. Simmons") reprising his role as [J. Jonah Jameson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Jonah_Jameson_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "J. Jonah Jameson (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in a video where he speaks out against Spider-Man before asking viewers to "like and subscribe".[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DailyBugle-100)[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DailyBugle2-101) In December 2020, Marvel Studios announced _[I Am Groot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I\_Am\_Groot "I Am Groot")_, a series of [photorealistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photorealism "Photorealism") animated shorts starring [Baby Groot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baby_Groot_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Baby Groot (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") for Disney+.[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IAmGroot-102)[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DisneyInvestorDayVerge-103)[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IAmGrootPhotoreal-104)

### Business practices

[![Image 9](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Joss_Whedon_by_Gage_Skidmore_7.jpg/250px-Joss_Whedon_by_Gage_Skidmore_7.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Joss_Whedon_by_Gage_Skidmore_7.jpg)

[Joss Whedon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joss_Whedon "Joss Whedon") was a significant contributor to the MCU's Phase Two: he offered creative insight to all of the films; launched the first MCU television series, _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._; and wrote and directed the crossover film _Avengers: Age of Ultron_.

In November 2016, Feige explained that the studio would often put together a "lookbook" of influences from the comics and art by Marvel's visual development department, to create a visual template for a project. These are put together at company retreats, which the studio holds approximately every 18 months to plan out future projects and develop the phases of the MCU. However, these lookbooks are not always shown to directors, with Marvel sometimes preferring to let the director offer their own ideas first.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeRetreats-105) When choosing a director for a project, Marvel Studios looks for filmmakers to hire who can guide a film.[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FastCompany-106) Some of their choices for directors have been considered "out-of-left-field" based on those directors' previous work. On this, Feige remarked that "you don't have to have directed a big, giant visual-effects movie to do a big, giant visual-effects movie for us. You just have to have done something singularly sort of awesome."[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ChooseDirector-107)

The studio ensures directors are open to the idea of the shared universe and are willing to include connective material, such as [Kenneth Branagh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenneth_Branagh "Kenneth Branagh") and [Joe Johnston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Johnston "Joe Johnston") needing to include scenes that set-up _[The Avengers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Avengers\_(2012\_film) "The Avengers (2012 film)")_ (2012) in their respective Phase One films _[Thor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thor\_(film) "Thor (film)")_ and _[Captain America: The First Avenger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_America:\_The\_First\_Avenger "Captain America: The First Avenger")_ (both 2011).[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BostonApril2012-5) Marvel Studios usually has a big idea they would like to explore or build to in a project, such as [Hydra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydra_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Hydra (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") infiltrating [S.H.I.E.L.D.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S.H.I.E.L.D._(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "S.H.I.E.L.D. (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in _[Captain America: The Winter Soldier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_America:\_The\_Winter\_Soldier "Captain America: The Winter Soldier")_ (2014), but they leave it up to the filmmakers to interpret and "improv a little bit" to get that point.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-RussosCrave-108) After these ideas have been developed, the creative team then begins exploring ideas from other future projects to see how to make any larger universe connections.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-RussosDirectingProcess-109) For many of their early films, Feige was closely involved during a film's development before allowing filming to be overseen by lower-level studio executives. Feige would then become involved again during editing, when films could be entirely rewritten or reworked.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WSJMay2025-41) Feige described the company's approach as "plus-ing at every turn", where they are always trying to improve a project and include new suggestions rather than sticking to a set script. Feige said they would not start a film without a full script, but he was never satisfied with their scripts or finished films and always felt they could do better.[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeConferenceJul2025THR-54)

In August 2012, Marvel signed _The Avengers_ and _[Avengers: Age of Ultron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Age\_of\_Ultron "Avengers: Age of Ultron")_ (2015) director [Joss Whedon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joss_Whedon "Joss Whedon") to an exclusive contract through June 2015 for film and television. With the deal, Whedon contributed creatively to all of the Phase Two films and also developed _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._, the first television series set in the MCU.[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WhedonConsultDeal-110) In April 2017, _[Guardians of the Galaxy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardians\_of\_the\_Galaxy\_(film) "Guardians of the Galaxy (film)")_ (2014) and _[Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardians\_of\_the\_Galaxy\_Vol.\_2 "Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 2")_ (2017) writer and director [James Gunn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Gunn "James Gunn") revealed that he would be working with Marvel to help plan future stories for the [Guardians of the Galaxy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardians_of_the_Galaxy_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Guardians of the Galaxy (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") characters and the wider "Marvel Cosmic Universe",[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GunnVol3Confirm-111) although Gunn became the co-CEO of [DC Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DC_Studios "DC Studios") in November 2022 and signed a four-year deal to work exclusively on [DC Comics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DC_Comics "DC Comics")-based projects.[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GunnSafranDCStudios-112) For Phase Three, there was a large amount of collaboration between the filmmakers of the individual character films and the filmmakers of the crossover films _Avengers: Infinity War_ and _Avengers: Endgame_, which were directed by the [Russo brothers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo_brothers "Russo brothers") and written by [Christopher Markus and Stephen McFeely](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Markus_and_Stephen_McFeely "Christopher Markus and Stephen McFeely"). This was to ensure their storytelling aligned for the Infinity Saga's culmination.[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-RussosWritersPhase3-113)

Marvel Studios began contracting their actors for multiple films, including signing actor [Samuel L. Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson "Samuel L. Jackson") to a then-unprecedented nine-film contract.[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-THRFeb2009-114) Feige said the studio had all actors sign contracts for multiple films, with the normal number being for three or more, while the nine or twelve-film deals were rare.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeContracts-115) The actors' contracts also feature clauses that allow Marvel to use up to three minutes of an actor's performance from one film in another, which Marvel describes as "bridging material".[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CreativeCommittee2-19) By the start of Phase Four, Marvel Studios was no longer contracting actors for a large number of projects, with deal lengths varying for each actor and project. Feige said the studio was looking for actors who were excited to join the franchise and appear in multiple projects without being locked into contractual obligations. He also noted that they were starting to include theme park attractions in actors' deals.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ActorContractsJuly2021-116) By December 2020, because of the [impact COVID-19 had on theaters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_cinema#Exhibitors "Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on cinema") and film studios shifting away from theatrical releases, Marvel Studios began exploring updated contracts for actors, writers, directors, and producers to receive adjusted compensation in the event a film had to debut on Disney+ instead of in theaters. _[TheWrap](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TheWrap "TheWrap")_ reported that the new contracts would likely only apply to films about to enter production.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WrapNewContractsDec2020-117)

For Marvel Television, Loeb said he and his executives were involved in all aspects of production: "whether it's being in the writers' room, editing, on set, casting—every step of the production goes through the Marvel team to tell the best story that we can". He said the studio was able to work on so many series across different networks and platforms because all they needed was one person working on each series to help "guide the process".[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LoebJul2017-118) When developing the crossover miniseries _The Defenders_, showrunner Marco Ramirez consulted with the creators of all the individual Marvel Netflix series, having them read each of the scripts for _The Defenders_ and provide insight into individual characters' worlds.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-RamirezEWJan2017-119) Actors appearing in Marvel Television series, such as [Charlie Cox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Cox "Charlie Cox") (who portrayed [Matt Murdock / Daredevil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matt_Murdock_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Matt Murdock (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in _Daredevil_) and [Adrianne Palicki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adrianne_Palicki "Adrianne Palicki") ([Bobbi Morse / Mockingbird](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bobbi_Morse_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Bobbi Morse (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._), were contractually obliged to appear in a Marvel Studios film if asked.[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CoxFilms-120)[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PalickiFilms-121)[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PalickiFilms2-122) In December 2021, Feige confirmed that Cox would reprise the role of Daredevil in Marvel Studios MCU productions,[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CoxMarvelStudios-123) with Cox first reprising the role in the film _[Spider-Man: No Way Home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_No\_Way\_Home "Spider-Man: No Way Home")_ (2021). Additionally, [Vincent D'Onofrio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vincent_D%27Onofrio "Vincent D'Onofrio") first reprised his role as [Wilson Fisk / Kingpin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilson_Fisk_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Wilson Fisk (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") from _Daredevil_ in the Disney+ series _[Hawkeye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawkeye\_(miniseries) "Hawkeye (miniseries)")_ (2021).[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-D'OnofrioCoxReprise-124)

Feature films
-------------

For a more comprehensive list, see [List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films "List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films").

Marvel Studios releases its films in groups called "Phases",[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DailyDotPhases-12)[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DigitalSpyPhases-13) with three phases making up a "Saga".[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeConferenceJul2025TotalFilm-59)

### The Infinity Saga

Further information: [Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_One "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One"), [Phase Two](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Two "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Two"), and [Phase Three](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Three "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Three")

The first three phases are collectively known as "The Infinity Saga".[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FFHInfinitySaga-22)[Phase One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_One "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One") consists of _[Iron Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron\_Man\_(2008\_film) "Iron Man (2008 film)")_ (2008), _[The Incredible Hulk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Incredible\_Hulk\_(film) "The Incredible Hulk (film)")_ (2008), _[Iron Man 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron\_Man\_2 "Iron Man 2")_ (2010), _[Thor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thor\_(film) "Thor (film)")_ (2011), and _[Captain America: The First Avenger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_America:\_The\_First\_Avenger "Captain America: The First Avenger")_ (2011), and concludes with the [crossover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fictional_crossover "Fictional crossover") film _[The Avengers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Avengers\_(2012\_film) "The Avengers (2012 film)")_ (2012). [Phase Two](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Two "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Two") comprises _[Iron Man 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron\_Man\_3 "Iron Man 3")_ (2013), _[Thor: The Dark World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thor:\_The\_Dark\_World "Thor: The Dark World")_ (2013), _[Captain America: The Winter Soldier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_America:\_The\_Winter\_Soldier "Captain America: The Winter Soldier")_ (2014), _[Guardians of the Galaxy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardians\_of\_the\_Galaxy\_(film) "Guardians of the Galaxy (film)")_ (2014), _[Avengers: Age of Ultron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Age\_of\_Ultron "Avengers: Age of Ultron")_ (2015), and _[Ant-Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant-Man\_(film) "Ant-Man (film)")_ (2015). _[Captain America: Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_America:\_Civil\_War "Captain America: Civil War")_ (2016) is the first film of [Phase Three](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Three "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Three"), and is followed by _[Doctor Strange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctor\_Strange\_(2016\_film) "Doctor Strange (2016 film)")_ (2016), _[Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardians\_of\_the\_Galaxy\_Vol.\_2 "Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 2")_ (2017), _[Spider-Man: Homecoming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_Homecoming "Spider-Man: Homecoming")_ (2017), _[Thor: Ragnarok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thor:\_Ragnarok "Thor: Ragnarok")_ (2017), _[Black Panther](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black\_Panther\_(film) "Black Panther (film)")_ (2018), _[Avengers: Infinity War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Infinity\_War "Avengers: Infinity War")_ (2018), _[Ant-Man and the Wasp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant-Man\_and\_the\_Wasp "Ant-Man and the Wasp")_ (2018), _[Captain Marvel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_Marvel\_(film) "Captain Marvel (film)")_ (2019), _[Avengers: Endgame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Endgame "Avengers: Endgame")_ (2019), and _[Spider-Man: Far From Home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_Far\_From\_Home "Spider-Man: Far From Home")_ (2019).[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DigitalSpyPhases-13)

### The Multiverse Saga

Further information: [Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Four](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Four "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Four"), [Phase Five](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Five "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Five"), and [Phase Six](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Six "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Six")

The second three phases are collectively known as "The Multiverse Saga", and include television series on [Disney+](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+").[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SDCC2022-36)[Phase Four](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Four "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Four") includes _[Black Widow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black\_Widow\_(2021\_film) "Black Widow (2021 film)")_ (2021), _[Shang-Chi and the Legend of the Ten Rings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shang-Chi\_and\_the\_Legend\_of\_the\_Ten\_Rings "Shang-Chi and the Legend of the Ten Rings")_ (2021), _[Eternals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eternals\_(film) "Eternals (film)")_ (2021), _[Spider-Man: No Way Home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_No\_Way\_Home "Spider-Man: No Way Home")_ (2021), _[Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctor\_Strange\_in\_the\_Multiverse\_of\_Madness "Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness")_ (2022), _[Thor: Love and Thunder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thor:\_Love\_and\_Thunder "Thor: Love and Thunder")_ (2022), and _[Black Panther: Wakanda Forever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black\_Panther:\_Wakanda\_Forever "Black Panther: Wakanda Forever")_ (2022). [Phase Five](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Five "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Five") includes _[Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant-Man\_and\_the\_Wasp:\_Quantumania "Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania")_ (2023), _[Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardians\_of\_the\_Galaxy\_Vol.\_3 "Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 3")_ (2023), _[The Marvels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Marvels "The Marvels")_ (2023), _[Deadpool & Wolverine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deadpool\_%26\_Wolverine "Deadpool & Wolverine")_ (2024), _[Captain America: Brave New World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_America:\_Brave\_New\_World "Captain America: Brave New World")_ (2025), and _[Thunderbolts*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thunderbolts* "Thunderbolts*")_ (2025). [Phase Six](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Six "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Six") includes _[The Fantastic Four: First Steps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Fantastic\_Four:\_First\_Steps "The Fantastic Four: First Steps")_ (2025), _[Spider-Man: Brand New Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_Brand\_New\_Day "Spider-Man: Brand New Day")_ (2026), _[Avengers: Doomsday](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Doomsday "Avengers: Doomsday")_ (2026), and _[Avengers: Secret Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers:\_Secret\_Wars "Avengers: Secret Wars")_ (2027).[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DigitalSpyPhases-13)

Television series and specials
------------------------------

For a more comprehensive list, see [List of Marvel Cinematic Universe television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_television_series "List of Marvel Cinematic Universe television series").

### Marvel Television series

Further information: [Marvel's ABC television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel%27s_ABC_television_series "Marvel's ABC television series"), [Marvel's Netflix television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel%27s_Netflix_television_series "Marvel's Netflix television series"), [Marvel's young adult television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel%27s_young_adult_television_series "Marvel's young adult television series"), and [Adventure into Fear (franchise)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adventure_into_Fear_(franchise) "Adventure into Fear (franchise)")

[Marvel Television](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Television "Marvel Television") produced multiple television series set in the MCU across broadcast, streaming, and cable. Its [ABC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company "American Broadcasting Company") series included _[Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agents\_of\_S.H.I.E.L.D. "Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.")_ (2013–2020), _[Agent Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent\_Carter\_(TV\_series) "Agent Carter (TV series)")_ (2015–2016), and _[Inhumans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inhumans\_(TV\_series) "Inhumans (TV series)")_ (2017); its [Netflix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netflix "Netflix") series included _[Daredevil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daredevil\_(TV\_series) "Daredevil (TV series)")_ (2015–2018), _[Jessica Jones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jessica\_Jones\_(TV\_series) "Jessica Jones (TV series)")_ (2015–2019), _[Luke Cage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luke\_Cage\_(TV\_series) "Luke Cage (TV series)")_ (2016–2018), _[Iron Fist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron\_Fist\_(TV\_series) "Iron Fist (TV series)")_ (2017–2018), the crossover miniseries _[The Defenders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Defenders\_(miniseries) "The Defenders (miniseries)")_ (2017), and _[The Punisher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Punisher\_(TV\_series) "The Punisher (TV series)")_ (2017–2019); its young adult series included _[Runaways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Runaways\_(TV\_series) "Runaways (TV series)")_ (2017–2019) streaming on [Hulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulu "Hulu") and _[Cloak & Dagger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloak\_%26\_Dagger\_(TV\_series) "Cloak & Dagger (TV series)")_ (2018–2019) airing on [Freeform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freeform_(TV_channel) "Freeform (TV channel)"); and the Hulu series _[Helstrom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helstrom\_(TV\_series) "Helstrom (TV series)")_ (2020) was originally intended to be the start of a planned "Adventure into Fear" franchise,[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LoebAug2019-125) but was ultimately "not tied to the MCU", according to showrunner [Paul Zbyszewski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Zbyszewski "Paul Zbyszewski").[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-HelstromNoMCU-126)

### Marvel Studios series

Further information: [Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Four §Television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Four#Television_series "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Four"), [Phase Five § Television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Five#Television_series "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Five"), [Phase Six § Television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_Six#Television_series "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase Six"), and [Marvel Studios Special Presentations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Studios_Special_Presentations "Marvel Studios Special Presentations")

Beginning with Phase Four, television series were included as part of the Phases in addition to their feature films. Each series is released on Disney+. Phase Four includes the series _[WandaVision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WandaVision "WandaVision")_ (2021), _[The Falcon and the Winter Soldier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Falcon\_and\_the\_Winter\_Soldier "The Falcon and the Winter Soldier")_ (2021), the [first season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loki_season_1 "Loki season 1") of _[Loki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loki\_(TV\_series) "Loki (TV series)")_ (2021), the [first season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/What_If...%3F_season_1 "What If...? season 1") of the animated series _[What If...?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/What\_If...%3F\_(TV\_series) "What If...? (TV series)")_ (2021), _[Hawkeye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawkeye\_(miniseries) "Hawkeye (miniseries)")_ (2021), _[Moon Knight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon\_Knight\_(miniseries) "Moon Knight (miniseries)")_ (2022), _[Ms. Marvel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ms.\_Marvel\_(miniseries) "Ms. Marvel (miniseries)")_ (2022), and _[She-Hulk: Attorney at Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/She-Hulk:\_Attorney\_at\_Law "She-Hulk: Attorney at Law")_ (2022). The television specials _[Werewolf by Night](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Werewolf\_by\_Night\_(TV\_special) "Werewolf by Night (TV special)")_ (2022) and _[The Guardians of the Galaxy Holiday Special](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Guardians\_of\_the\_Galaxy\_Holiday\_Special "The Guardians of the Galaxy Holiday Special")_ (2022) are also included in the phase. Phase Five includes _[Secret Invasion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secret\_Invasion\_(miniseries) "Secret Invasion (miniseries)")_ (2023), the [second season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loki_season_2 "Loki season 2") of _Loki_ (2023), the [second season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/What_If...%3F_season_2 "What If...? season 2") of _What If...?_ (2023), _[Echo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Echo\_(miniseries) "Echo (miniseries)")_ (2024), _[Agatha All Along](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agatha\_All\_Along "Agatha All Along")_ (2024), the [third season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/What_If...%3F_season_3 "What If...? season 3") of _What If...?_ (2024), the [first season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Your_Friendly_Neighborhood_Spider-Man_season_1 "Your Friendly Neighborhood Spider-Man season 1") of the animated series _[Your Friendly Neighborhood Spider-Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Your\_Friendly\_Neighborhood\_Spider-Man "Your Friendly Neighborhood Spider-Man")_ (2025), the [first season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daredevil:_Born_Again_season_1 "Daredevil: Born Again season 1") of _[Daredevil: Born Again](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daredevil:\_Born\_Again "Daredevil: Born Again")_ (2025), and _[Ironheart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ironheart\_(miniseries) "Ironheart (miniseries)")_ (2025). Phase Six includes the animated miniseries _[Eyes of Wakanda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eyes\_of\_Wakanda "Eyes of Wakanda")_ (2025) and _[Marvel Zombies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel\_Zombies\_(miniseries) "Marvel Zombies (miniseries)")_ (2025), _[Wonder Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wonder\_Man\_(miniseries) "Wonder Man (miniseries)")_ (2026), the [second](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daredevil:_Born_Again_season_2 "Daredevil: Born Again season 2") and [third seasons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daredevil:_Born_Again_season_3 "Daredevil: Born Again season 3") of _Born Again_ (2026–27), and _[VisionQuest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VisionQuest "VisionQuest")_ (2026).[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DigitalSpyPhases-13)[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DDBAS3Release-127) An [untitled Punisher television special](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Untitled_Punisher_television_special "Untitled Punisher television special") (2026) is also expected to be released during the phase.[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PunisherSpecialRelease-128)

Short films
-----------

### Marvel One-Shots

Main articles: [Marvel One-Shots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_One-Shots "Marvel One-Shots") and [_Team Thor_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Team_Thor "Team Thor")

[Marvel One-Shots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_One-Shots "Marvel One-Shots") are a series of [direct-to-video](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct-to-video "Direct-to-video")[short films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short_film "Short film") that are included as special features in the MCU films' [Blu-ray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc "Blu-ray Disc") and [digital distribution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_distribution "Digital distribution") releases.
