The films included _[The Consultant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Consultant\_(film) "The Consultant (film)")_ (2011), _[A Funny Thing Happened on the Way to Thor's Hammer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A\_Funny\_Thing\_Happened\_on\_the\_Way\_to\_Thor%27s\_Hammer "A Funny Thing Happened on the Way to Thor's Hammer")_ (2011),[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-OneShotsAnnouncement-94)_[Item 47](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Item\_47 "Item 47")_ (2012),[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Item47-129)_[Agent Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent\_Carter\_(film) "Agent Carter (film)")_ (2013),[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CBRCarter-130) and _[All Hail the King](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All\_Hail\_the\_King "All Hail the King")_ (2014).[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AHTK-131)

Following the One-Shots becoming available on Disney+ in January 2022, Marvel classified the _[Team Thor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Team\_Thor "Team Thor")_[mockumentary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mockumentary "Mockumentary") shorts as One-Shots.[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-OneShotsD+Release-132)[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-TeamThorOneShots-133)[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-TeamThorOneShotsD+Tweet-134)_Team Thor_ is a series of direct-to-video mockumentary short films that were released from 2016 to 2018, consisting of _Team Thor_, _Team Thor: Part 2_, and _Team Darryl_, all written and directed by [Taika Waititi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taika_Waititi "Taika Waititi").[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-TeamThor-135)[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-TeamThorPart2-136)[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-TeamDarryl-137)

### _I Am Groot_

Main article: [_I Am Groot_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I_Am_Groot "I Am Groot")

_I Am Groot_ is a series of [photorealistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photorealism "Photorealism") animated short films for Disney+ starring [Baby Groot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baby_Groot_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Baby Groot (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") going on adventures with new and unusual characters.[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IAmGroot-102)[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DisneyInvestorDayVerge-103)[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IAmGrootPhotoreal-104)[Vin Diesel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vin_Diesel "Vin Diesel") reprises his role, with five shorts releasing on August 10, 2022.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IAmGrootRelease-138) A second season with five additional shorts was released on September 6, 2023.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IAmGrootS2Release-139)

Other media
-----------

### Digital series

_[WHIH Newsfront](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WHIH\_Newsfront "WHIH Newsfront")_ (2015–16) is an in-universe current affairs show that serves as a [viral marketing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_marketing "Viral marketing") campaign for some of the MCU films, created in partnership with Google for [YouTube](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube "YouTube").[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WHIHPromo-98)[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BibbReveal-140) The campaign is an extension of the fictional news network WHIH World News, which is seen reporting on major events in many MCU films and television series.[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WHIHWorldNews-141)[Leslie Bibb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leslie_Bibb "Leslie Bibb") reprises her role as [Christine Everhart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christine_Everhart_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Christine Everhart (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") from the _Iron Man_ films.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BibbReveal-140)

_[Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.: Slingshot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agents\_of\_S.H.I.E.L.D.:\_Slingshot "Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.: Slingshot")_ (2016) is one of several [_Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._ web series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agents_of_S.H.I.E.L.D._web_series "Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D. web series") created for [ABC.com](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ABC.com "ABC.com") and produced by Marvel Television that is a supplement to _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._, with the main cast reprising their roles.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Slingshot-99)

The first two seasons of _[The Daily Bugle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Daily\_Bugle\_(web\_series) "The Daily Bugle (web series)")_ (2019–2022) are an in-universe current affairs show serving as a viral marketing campaign for the films _Spider-Man: Far From Home_ and _Spider-Man: No Way Home_, with the videos released on YouTube and [TikTok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TikTok "TikTok"). It is based on the fictional sensationalist news outlet [of the same name](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TheDailyBugle.net "TheDailyBugle.net") that appears in the MCU—itself based on the fictional newspaper agency [of the same name](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daily_Bugle "Daily Bugle") appearing in several [Marvel Comics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Comics "Marvel Comics") publications. [J. K. Simmons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._K._Simmons "J. K. Simmons") and [Angourie Rice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angourie_Rice "Angourie Rice") reprise their roles as [J. Jonah Jameson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Jonah_Jameson_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "J. Jonah Jameson (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") and [Betty Brant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Betty_Brant_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Betty Brant (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") from the _Spider-Man_ films.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DailyBugleTikTok-142)

### Comic books

Main article: [Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_tie-in_comics "Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics")

Multiple [limited series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limited_series_(comics) "Limited series (comics)") or [one-shot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-shot_(comics) "One-shot (comics)") comic books that tie into the MCU films and television series have been published by Marvel Comics. They are intended to tell additional stories about existing characters or to make connections between MCU projects, without necessarily expanding the universe or introducing new concepts or characters.[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IM2comics-92)[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-TieInComics2-143)

### Books

For books written about the MCU, see [§Literary material](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#Literary_material) below.

_The Wakanda Files: A Technological Exploration of the Avengers and Beyond_ is "a collection of papers, articles, blueprints, and notes amassed throughout history by Wakanda's War Dogs" at the request of [Shuri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shuri_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Shuri (Marvel Cinematic Universe)"). It is organized by areas of study and covers the technological advancements throughout the MCU. The book, which exists within the universe, was written by Troy Benjamin and published by Epic Ink and Quarto Publishing Group. _The Wakanda Files_ has content printed with UV ink that can be viewed with Kimoyo bead–shaped UV lights included with the book. It was released on October 20, 2020.[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WakandaFiles-144)

_[Look Out for the Little Guy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Look\_Out\_for\_the\_Little\_Guy "Look Out for the Little Guy")_, the fictional memoir written by [Scott Lang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scott_Lang_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Scott Lang (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") as seen in _Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania_, was released by [Hyperion Avenue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disney_Publishing_Worldwide "Disney Publishing Worldwide") on September 5, 2023. It was created alongside Marvel Studios and the _Quantumania_ filmmakers,[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LookOutForTheLittleGuy-145) and was written by [Rob Kutner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rob_Kutner "Rob Kutner"),[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LoftLGAuthors-146) featuring "over 20 short pieces exploring different aspects of Scott's experiences" as a father and Avenger.[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LookOutForTheLittleGuy-145)_Quantumania_ writer [Jeff Loveness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeff_Loveness "Jeff Loveness") wrote the material from the memoir that was featured in the film.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LoftLGAuthors-146)

### Music

Main article: [Music of the Marvel Cinematic Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_of_the_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe "Music of the Marvel Cinematic Universe")

Various composers have created the [film and television scores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film_score "Film score") of the MCU films, television series, One-Shots, Special Presentations, and other related projects of the MCU, primarily released by Marvel Studios's record label [Marvel Music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Music_(record_label) "Marvel Music (record label)"). Original songs have also been created specifically for use in the franchise, while [Brian Tyler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Tyler "Brian Tyler") and [Michael Giacchino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Giacchino "Michael Giacchino") have both scored [fanfares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fanfares "Fanfares") for the Marvel Studios [production logo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Production_logo "Production logo").[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FanfareTyler-147)[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FanfareGiacchino-148)

Fictional universe
------------------

### Timeline

Main article: [Marvel Cinematic Universe timeline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_timeline "Marvel Cinematic Universe timeline")

The fictional timeline of the MCU includes the feature films, television series, television specials, short films, and the _I Am Groot_ shorts from Marvel Studios and Marvel Television's Netflix series. While the early films of Phase One and Phase Two of the franchise followed each other in the timeline similar to their release order, Phase Three saw many of the films overlapping with each other in the timeline, while also introducing the first prequel property, _Captain Marvel_. The Phase Three film _Avengers: Endgame_ featured characters traveling into the past and introduced a five-year time jump, with many subsequent releases in Phase Four and Phase Five set after _Endgame_'s events in the timeline. The television series _Loki_ and _What If...?_ were the first properties to occur outside of the main timeline and explore alternative timelines and universes.

There have been numerous attempts by Marvel Studios and others to codify the events of the MCU, which have been subject to perceived [continuity errors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuity_errors "Continuity errors"), resulting in Marvel Studios releasing an official timeline book in 2023 for their first four phases that were designated as part of their "[Sacred Timeline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacred_Timeline "Sacred Timeline")". This book did not feature projects produced by other companies, such as Marvel Television's series, which were all loosely connected to the films; however, it was noted that all of these outside projects were part of the larger Marvel canon. In early 2024, Marvel Studios formally integrated Marvel Television's group of Netflix series into its Disney+ timeline.

As of the Phase Five television series _Daredevil: Born Again_ and the film _Thunderbolts*_, the "present day" in the MCU is 2027.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DDBATimeline2-149)[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ThunderboltsTimeline-150) The following covers and discusses MCU media released by Marvel Studios and the Netflix series by Marvel Television. _Loki_ and _What If...?_ are excluded from the diagram because they occur outside of the main timeline. _Werewolf by Night_ is also excluded, given that the special explicitly does not indicate where it takes place in the MCU. Disney+'s timeline order places the first seasons of _Loki_ and _What If...?_ between _Avengers: Endgame_ and _WandaVision_, their second seasons after _The Marvels_, and _Werewolf by Night_ after _Thor: Love and Thunder_; _Werewolf by Night_ is also placed here in _[The Marvel Cinematic Universe: An Official Timeline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Marvel\_Cinematic\_Universe:\_An\_Official\_Timeline "The Marvel Cinematic Universe: An Official Timeline")_.

**Key**: 
*   Occurs on the MCU's Sacred Timeline 
*   Occurs outside the MCU's Sacred Timeline at a set timeframe

### Multiverse

Main article: [Multiverse (Marvel Cinematic Universe)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiverse_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Multiverse (Marvel Cinematic Universe)")

The _[Official Handbook of the Marvel Universe A to Z](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official\_Handbook\_of\_the\_Marvel\_Universe\_A\_to\_Z "Official Handbook of the Marvel Universe A to Z")_, Vol. 5, published in 2008, originally designated the Marvel Cinematic Universe as Earth-199999 within the [continuity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuity_(fiction) "Continuity (fiction)") of Marvel's comic [multiverse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiverse_(Marvel_Comics) "Multiverse (Marvel Comics)"), a collection of fictional alternate universes, although, this designation was rarely used officially outside of the source material.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Earth-199999-215) The television series _Loki_ and _What If...?_ were the first to explore the concept of the multiverse within the MCU,[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LokiTimeline-216)[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WhatIfTimeline-217) as well as the film _Spider-Man: No Way Home_, which connected the MCU to other [Spider-Man film franchises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man_in_film "Spider-Man in film") by featuring characters from [Sam Raimi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sam_Raimi "Sam Raimi")'s [_Spider-Man_ trilogy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man_(2002_film_series) "Spider-Man (2002 film series)") (2002–2007), [Marc Webb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marc_Webb "Marc Webb")'s [_The Amazing Spider-Man_ films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(film_series) "The Amazing Spider-Man (film series)") (2012–14), and [Sony's Spider-Man Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sony%27s_Spider-Man_Universe "Sony's Spider-Man Universe") (SSU).[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-NWHSMTASM-218)[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PostCreditsVenom-219) The SSU film _[Venom: Let There Be Carnage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venom:\_Let\_There\_Be\_Carnage "Venom: Let There Be Carnage")_ (2021) briefly featured the main universe of the MCU as well.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PostCreditsVenom-219) In _Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness_, the main universe of MCU events was designated as [Earth-616](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth-616_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Earth-616 (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") (a designation first referenced in _Spider-Man: Far From Home_), sharing the name of the [main Marvel Comics universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth-616 "Earth-616"), while another universe was designated as [Earth-838](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth-838 "Earth-838").[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MoMUniverses-220) Sony's animated film _[Spider-Man: Across the Spider-Verse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_Across\_the\_Spider-Verse "Spider-Man: Across the Spider-Verse")_ (2023) references the events of _No Way Home_, citing the MCU's primary reality as Earth-199999.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AcrossTheSpiderVerse199999-221)[20th Century Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/20th_Century_Fox "20th Century Fox")'s [_X-Men_ film series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-Men_(film_series) "X-Men (film series)") (2000–2020) is designated as Earth-10005 in _Deadpool & Wolverine_.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DPWYearEarth-187) That film features several actors reprising their roles from the _X-Men_ film series along with characters from Fox's films _[Daredevil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daredevil\_(film) "Daredevil (film)")_ (2003) and its [spin-off](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin-off_(media) "Spin-off (media)")_[Elektra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elektra\_(2005\_film) "Elektra (2005 film)")_ (2005), _[Fantastic Four](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantastic\_Four\_(2005\_film) "Fantastic Four (2005 film)")_ (2005) and its sequel _[Fantastic Four: Rise of the Silver Surfer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantastic\_Four:\_Rise\_of\_the\_Silver\_Surfer "Fantastic Four: Rise of the Silver Surfer")_ (2007), and [New Line Cinema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Line_Cinema "New Line Cinema")'s [_Blade_ film trilogy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blade_(franchise) "Blade (franchise)") (1994–2004).[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DPWVoidCameos-222)[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DPWEWCameos-223) Phases Four, Five, and Six comprise "[The Multiverse Saga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Multiverse_Saga "The Multiverse Saga")".[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SDCC2022-36)

With the release of _The Marvel Cinematic Universe: An Official Timeline_ in October 2023, Feige wrote in its [foreword](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreword "Foreword") that Marvel Studios only considered, at that time, projects developed by them in their first four phases as part of their "[Sacred Timeline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacred_Timeline "Sacred Timeline")", but acknowledged the history of [other Marvel films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_films_based_on_Marvel_Comics_publications "List of films based on Marvel Comics publications") and [television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_television_series_based_on_Marvel_Comics_publications "List of television series based on Marvel Comics publications") that would exist in the larger multiverse and said they were "canonical to Marvel".[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeTimelineBookQuote-224) In January 2024, Winderbaum acknowledged that Marvel Studios had previously been "a little bit cagey" about what was part of their Sacred Timeline, noting how there had been the corporate divide between what Marvel Studios created and what Marvel Television created. He continued that as time had passed, Marvel Studios began to see "how well integrated the [Marvel Television] stories are" and personally felt confident in saying Marvel Television's _Daredevil_ was part of the Sacred Timeline.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WinderbaumScreenRantJan2024-225)

List indicators

This section includes characters who will appear or have appeared in at least three MCU films/series and received main billing credit in at least two franchises.

*   A dark grey cell indicates the character was not in the media, or that the character's presence has not yet been confirmed.

*   A P indicates an appearance in onscreen photographs.
*   A V indicates a voice-only role.

Additionally, Paul Bettany was the first actor to portray two main characters within the universe, voicing Tony Stark's [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") J.A.R.V.I.S. and portraying Vision.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BettanyRoles-306)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BettanyRecurring-259) James D'Arcy was the first actor to reprise their role as a character introduced in an MCU television series in an MCU film, portraying Edwin Jarvis—the human inspiration for J.A.R.V.I.S.—in the series _[Agent Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent\_Carter\_(TV\_series) "Agent Carter (TV series)")_ (2015–16) and _Avengers: Endgame_.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-D'ArcyEndgame-260)[J. K. Simmons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._K._Simmons "J. K. Simmons") became the first actor to reprise a non-MCU role in the MCU when he appeared as [J. Jonah Jameson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Jonah_Jameson_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "J. Jonah Jameson (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") (a role he played in Sam Raimi's _Spider-Man_ trilogy from 2002 to 2007) in _Spider-Man: Far From Home_.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SimmonsFFH-307)

Prior to his death in 2018, Stan Lee, the creator or co-creator of many of the characters adapted in the MCU, made cameo appearances in [all of the feature films and television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Watchers%27_Informant "The Watchers' Informant") except _Inhumans_. In _Iron Fist_, it is revealed his on-set photograph cameo in the Marvel Netflix series is as [NYPD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Department "New York City Police Department") Captain [Irving Forbush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbush_Man "Forbush Man").[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LeeForbush-308) His cameo in _Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 2_ sees Lee appearing as an informant to the [Watchers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watcher_(comics) "Watcher (comics)"), discussing previous adventures that include Lee's cameos in other MCU films; he specifically mentions his time as a [FedEx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FedEx "FedEx") delivery man, referring to Lee's cameo in _Captain America: Civil War_.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LeeCameo3-309) This acknowledged the fan theory that Lee may be portraying the same character in all his cameos,[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LeeCameo2-310) with writer and director James Gunn noting that commentators believed Lee was portraying the character [Uatu the Watcher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uatu "Uatu") and "that all of these cameos are part of him being a [Watcher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watcher_(comics) "Watcher (comics)"). So, Stan Lee as a guy who is working for the Watchers was something that I thought was fun for the MCU."[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LeeCameo3-309)[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LeeCameo2-310) Feige added that Lee "clearly exists, you know, above and apart from the reality of all the films. So the notion that he could be sitting there on a cosmic pit stop during the jump gate sequence in _Guardians_...really says, so wait a minute, he's this same character who's popped up in all these films?"[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LeeCameo-311) Following Lee's death, Marvel Studios chose not to create any new Lee cameos in future projects.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-StanLeeCameoPolicy-312)[NY1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NY1 "NY1") news anchor [Pat Kiernan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Kiernan "Pat Kiernan") has also appeared in multiple MCU films and television series as himself.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Kiernan-313)

Reception
---------

Main article: [Reception of the Marvel Cinematic Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reception_of_the_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe "Reception of the Marvel Cinematic Universe")

Early on, the shared universe element of the Marvel Cinematic Universe was criticized by some journalists. Around the release of _The Avengers_ in 2012, Jim Vorel of _[Herald & Review](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herald\_%26\_Review "Herald & Review")_ called the Marvel Cinematic Universe "complicated" and "impressive", but said, "As more and more heroes get their own film adaptations, the overall universe becomes increasingly confusing."[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Herald&Review-314) Kofi Outlaw of _Screen Rant_ stated that while _The Avengers_ was a success, "Marvel Studios still has room to improve their approach to building a shared movie universe".[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ScreenRant_2013-06-27-315) Some reviewers criticized the fact that the desire to create a shared universe led to films that did not hold as well on their own. In his review of _Thor: The Dark World_, _[Forbes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")_ critic Scott Mendelson likened the MCU to "a glorified television series", with _The Dark World_ being a "'stand-alone' episode that contains little long-range mythology".[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ForbesMCUReception-316) Collider's Matt Goldberg considered that while _Iron Man 2_, _Thor_ and _Captain America: The First Avenger_ were quality productions, "they have never really been their own movies", feeling that the plot detours to S.H.I.E.L.D. or lead-ups to _The Avengers_ dragged down the films' narratives.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ColliderMCUReception-317)

The metaphor of the MCU as "the world's biggest TV show" was discussed again, after the release of _Captain America: Civil War_, by [Emily St. James](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emily_St._James "Emily St. James") of _[Vox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vox\_(website) "Vox (website)")_, who felt that film in particular highlighted Marvel's success with the model, saying, "Viewed in complete isolation, the plot of _Captain America: Civil War_ makes little to no sense ... [but] when you think about where [Captain America] has been in earlier Marvel films ... his leeriness about being subject to oversight makes a lot more sense." St. James continued that when thinking about the MCU as a television series, many "common criticisms people tend to level at it take on a new context" such as complaints that the films are formulaic, lack "visual spark", or "shoehorn in story elements" that "are necessary to set up future films", all characteristics that "are fairly typical on television, where a director's influence is much lower than that of the showrunner", in this case, Feige. Comparing the films to the series _Game of Thrones_ specifically, St. James noted that each solo film checks "in on various characters and their individual side stories, before bringing everyone together in the finale (or, rather, an Avengers film)", with _Guardians of the Galaxy_ being equivalent to the character [Daenerys Targaryen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daenerys_Targaryen "Daenerys Targaryen")—"both separated by long distances from everybody else". She noted that this format was an extension of early "TV-like" film franchises such as _[Star Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star\_Wars "Star Wars")_, as well as the format of the comics upon which the films are based. "I say all of this not to suggest that film franchises resembling TV series is necessarily a good trend", St. James concluded, "For as much as I generally enjoy the Marvel movies, I'm disheartened by the possibility that their particular form might take over the film industry ... But I also don't think it's the end of the world if Marvel continues on ... there's a reason TV has stolen so much of the cultural conversation over the past few decades. There's something legitimately exciting about the way the medium tells stories when it's good, and if nothing else, Marvel's success shows the film world could learn from that."[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VoxCivilWarTV-318)

Following the conclusion of season one of _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._, Mary McNamara at the _[Los Angeles Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los\_Angeles\_Times "Los Angeles Times")_ praised the connections between that series and the films, stating that "never before has television been literally married to film, charged with filling in the back story and creating the connective tissue of an ongoing film franchise ... [_Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._] is now not only a very good show in its own right, it's part of Marvel's multiplatform city-state. It faces a future of perpetual re-invention, and that puts it in the exhilarating first car of television's roller-coaster ride toward possible world domination."[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LATimesSHIELDReview-319) Terri Schwartz of Zap2it agreed with this sentiment, stating that "the fact that [_Captain America: The Winter Soldier_] so influenced the show is game-changing in terms of how the mediums of film and television can be interwoven", though "the fault there seems to be that _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._ had to bide time until _The Winter Soldier_'s release", which led to much criticism.[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Zap2itSHIELDReview-320)

In January 2015, Michael Doran of [Newsarama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newsarama "Newsarama") and Graeme McMillian of _The Hollywood Reporter_ had a "point-counterpoint" debate in response to the first _Ant-Man_ trailer. Doran stated, "Marvel has raised the bar _sooo_ high that as opposed to just allowing another film to finish under the [MCU] bar, we're all overly and perhaps even eager to overreact to the first thing that doesn't clear it". McMillian responded, "at this point, Marvel's brand is such that I'm not sure it can offer up something like [the trailer] _without_ it seeming like a crushing disappointment ... part of Marvel's brand is that it _doesn't_ offer the kind of run-of-the-mill superhero movie that you're talking about, that it's ... at least different enough to tweak and play with the genre somehow ... The fact that there's such upset about this trailer being ... well, okay ... suggests to me that the audience _is_ expecting something to knock their socks off." Doran concluded, "That does seem to be the point here—the expectations fans now have for everything Marvel Studios ... [and] Marvel _is_ going to eventually falter."[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-NewsaramaDiscussionJan2015-321)

After seeing the portrayal of [Yellowjacket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darren_Cross_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Darren Cross (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in _Ant-Man_, the antagonist of the film, McMillian noted,

> It's hardly a secret that Marvel Studios has a bit of a problem when it comes to offering up exciting characters for their heroes to fight against ... [their] villains generally fall into one of two camps. There's the Unstoppable Monster ... or there's the Professional White Guy in a Suit with an Ego ... No matter which of the groups the above villains fall into, they share one common purpose: _evil_. The motivations for evil likely differ—although, invariably, they fall under the umbrella of 'misguided belief in a greater good that doesn't exist'—but that really doesn't matter, because without fail, there will be so little time in the movie to actually properly explore those motivations, meaning that to all intents and purposes, the villain is being evil for reasons of plot necessity and little else ... The strange thing about this is that Marvel's comic books offer a number of wonderful, colorful bad guys who could step outside the above parameters and offer an alternative to the formulaic villains audiences have gotten used to (and arguably bored with) ... In future movies, we can only hope [they are] treated in such a way that their freak flags are allowed to fly free.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-THRVillians-322)

Following the release of _Jessica Jones_, David Priest at _[CNET](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CNET "CNET")_ wrote about how the series rescues "Marvel from itself ... _Jessica Jones_ takes big steps forward in terms of theme, craft and diversity. It's a good story first, and a superhero show second. And for the first time, the MCU seems like it matters. Our culture needs stories like this. Here's hoping Marvel keeps them coming."[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CNETJJ-323) For Paul Tassi and Erik Kain of _Forbes_, watching the series made them question the MCU, with Kain feeling that the "morally complex, violent, dark world of _Jessica Jones_ has no place in the MCU ... right now, the MCU is holding back shows like _Jessica Jones_ and _Daredevil_, while those shows are contributing absolutely nothing to the MCU."[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-KainForbesJJ-324) Tassi went so far as to wonder what "the point of the Marvel Cinematic Universe" is, lamenting the lack of major crossovers in the franchise since the _Winter Soldier_ reveal on _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._, and saying that _Jessica Jones_ is "so far removed from the world of _The Avengers_, it might as well not be in the same universe at all ... [I] really don't understand the point of [the MCU] if they're going to keep everything within it separated off in these little boxes".[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-TassiForbesJJ-325) Conversely, Eric Francisco of Inverse called _Jessica Jones_'s lack of overt connections to the MCU "the show's chief advantage. Besides demonstrating how physically wide open the MCU's scope really is, _Jessica Jones_ also proves the MCU's thematic durability."[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-InverseJJ-326)

In April 2016, Marvel Studios revealed that [Alfre Woodard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfre_Woodard "Alfre Woodard") would appear in _Captain America: Civil War_, having already been cast as [Mariah Dillard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariah_Dillard_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Mariah Dillard (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in _Luke Cage_ the previous year.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WoodardSC-327) This "raised hopes that Marvel could be uniting its film and Netflix universes",[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WoodardIGN-328) with "one of the first and strongest connections" between the two.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WoodardSC-327)_Civil War_ writers Christopher Markus and Stephen McFeely revealed that Woodard would instead be portraying [Miriam Sharpe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miriam_Sharpe_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Miriam Sharpe (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") in the film, explaining that she had been cast on the suggestion of Robert Downey Jr., and they had not learned of her casting in _Luke Cage_ until afterwards.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WoodardSC-327) This was not the first instance of actors being cast in multiple roles in the MCU, but this casting was called more "significant", and seen by many as a "disappointing" indication of "the growing divide" and "lack of more satisfying cooperation" between Marvel Studios and Marvel Television following the September 2015 corporate reshuffling of Marvel Entertainment.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WoodardSC-327)[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WoodardSF-329)

Speaking to the 1990s setting of _[Captain Marvel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain\_Marvel\_(film) "Captain Marvel (film)")_, "the MCU's first full period piece since [Phase One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe:_Phase_One "Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One")'s _Captain America: The First Avenger_ in 2011", Richard Newby of _The Hollywood Reporter_ felt the return of younger versions of some characters introduced and killed in earlier films "open[ed] up the MCU in a whole new way and broaden[ed] the franchise's mantra of 'it's all connected'". Speaking specifically to [Clark Gregg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clark_Gregg "Clark Gregg")'s appearance as Agent Phil Coulson in the film, Newby noted the appearance "doesn't exactly mend fences between Marvel's film and TV divisions, [but] it does strengthen the connective tissue and the sense that these characters still matter in the grand scheme of Marvel's film plans". He also hoped that continuity from _Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D._ would be maintained in _Captain Marvel_, especially since Coulson has dealt with the Kree in the series. Newby also added that shifting to different time periods would help Marvel Studios "sustain this cinematic universe for the next 10 years" by allowing them to repeat some of the genres previously used, as they could then feel "fresh" and have "different rules and different restraints", as well as allow them to build upon material established in the television series such as _Agent Carter_. He concluded,

> Marvel Studios has an entire sandbox to play in, but, for necessary reasons, has largely chosen to remain in a small corner in order to ground audiences in these concepts. Now that the basis has been laid, the opportunity for exploration in both film and television lies ahead, with _Captain Marvel_ leading the way. Wherever Marvel Studios plans to take the MCU in the future, it's refreshing to know that its past is expansive and filled with infinite possibilities.[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-THRMar2018CaptainMarvel-330)

Likewise, in his review of _Avengers: Endgame_, [Joe Morgenstern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Morgenstern "Joe Morgenstern") of _[The Wall Street Journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Wall\_Street\_Journal "The Wall Street Journal")_ acknowledged the unique achievement that the Marvel Cinematic Universe had accomplished:

> These are difficult times for big-screen entertainment. As the medium declines and TV grows ascendant, authentic spectacles—as opposed to lavish embellishments of smallish ideas—threaten to become a thing of the fabled past. All the more reason, then, to cherish what Marvel has achieved, even though befuddling stumbles have occurred along the way. The studio has kept the faith by smartening up most of its films, not dumbing them down, by banking on, and raking in profits from, the audience's appetite for surprise, its capacity for complexity. When the final battle comes at the end of _Avengers: Endgame_, it's inevitably unwieldy—every Marvel character you can think of from the past decade shows up for one more assault on cosmic evil—but thrilling all the same, and followed by a delicate [coda](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/coda "wikt:coda"). So many stories. So many adventures. So much to sort out before the next cycle starts.[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MorgensternEndgame-331)

Many famous filmmakers expressed different views both on the success and quality of MCU. In October 2019, filmmaker [Martin Scorsese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Scorsese "Martin Scorsese") openly criticized Marvel films in an interview and during a [David Lean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Lean "David Lean") lecture in London, later expanded in an [op-ed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Op-ed "Op-ed") in _[The New York Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_New\_York\_Times "The New York Times")_, asserting that these films are not cinema, but are instead the equivalent of theme park rides that lack "mystery, revelation or genuine emotional danger".[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ScorseseNotCinema-332)[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ScorseseNYTimes-333)[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ScorseseTalks-334) He also stated that such films are corporation products that have been "market-researched, audience-tested, vetted, modified, revetted and remodified until they're ready for consumption", and that the invasion of such "theme park" films in theaters crowded out films by other directors.[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ScorseseIndieWire-335) Scorsese's remarks were dismissed by directors of MCU films such as Joss Whedon and James Gunn,[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ScorseseNotCinema-332) while they were defended by [Francis Ford Coppola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francis_Ford_Coppola "Francis Ford Coppola"), who described the potential effect of Marvel films in the film industry as "despicable".[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CoppolaResponse-336) In September 2021, director [Denis Villeneuve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denis_Villeneuve "Denis Villeneuve") noted that Marvel films "are nothing more than a 'cut and paste' of others" that have "turned us into zombies a bit".[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VilleneuveSep2021-337) In February 2022, director [Roland Emmerich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roland_Emmerich "Roland Emmerich") felt large blockbuster films such as the MCU and _Star Wars_ films were "ruining our industry a little", since "nobody does anything original anymore".[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-EmmerichFeb2022-338) Conversely, [George Miller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Miller_(filmmaker) "George Miller (filmmaker)") stated, "To me, it's all cinema. I don't think you can ghettoize it and say, oh this is cinema or that is cinema. It applies to all the arts, to literature, the performing arts, painting and music, in all its form. It's such a broad spectrum, a wide range and to say that anyone is more significant or more important than the other, is missing the point. It's one big mosaic and each bit of work fits into it."[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MillerResponse-339)

Marvel's American audience was studied by [Morning Consult](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morning_Consult "Morning Consult") in 2021, which found that 9% of Marvel's fan base is [Generation Z](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generation_Z "Generation Z"), 64% of fans are [White](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_people "White people") adults, and 42% of fans live in [suburban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suburb "Suburb") areas.[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AudienceBreakdown-340) In 2023, critics began describing the volume of interconnected storylines as a "homework assignment".[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-Homework-341)

Cultural impact
---------------

### Other studios

After the release of _The Avengers_ in May 2012, Tom Russo of _[Boston.com](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston.com "Boston.com")_ noted that aside from the occasional "novelty" such as _[Alien vs. Predator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alien\_vs.\_Predator\_(film) "Alien vs. Predator (film)")_ (2004), the idea of a shared universe was virtually unheard of in Hollywood.[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-BostonApril2012-5) Since that time, the shared universe model created by Marvel Studios has begun to be replicated by other film studios that held rights to other comic book characters. In April 2014, Tuna Amobi, a media analyst for [Standard & Poor's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s "Standard & Poor's") Equity Research Services, stated that over the previous three to five years, Hollywood studios had begun planning "megafranchises" for years to come, rather than working on one blockbuster at a time. Amobi added, "A lot of these superhero characters were just being left there to gather dust. Disney has proved that this [approach and genre] can be a gold mine."[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ASM2EW-342) With more studios now "playing the megafranchise game", Doug Creutz, media analyst for [Cowen and Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cowen_and_Company "Cowen and Company"), feels the allure will eventually die for audiences: "If Marvel's going to make two or three films a year, and Warner Brothers is going to do at least a film every year, and Sony's going to do a film every year, and Fox [is] going to do a film every year, can everyone do well in that scenario? I'm not sure they can."[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ASM2EW-342)

In March 2018, Patrick Shanley of _The Hollywood Reporter_ opined that "the key differences between a regular franchise, such as _[The Fast and the Furious](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Fast\_and\_the\_Furious "The Fast and the Furious")_ or [_Pitch Perfect_ films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pitch_Perfect_(film_series) "Pitch Perfect (film series)"), and a shared universe is the amount of planning and interweaving that goes into each individual film. Its all too easy to make a film that exists solely for the purpose of setting up future installments and expanding a world, rather than a film that stands on its own merits while deftly hinting or winking at its place in the larger mythos. In that, the MCU has flourished." He felt that _Iron Man_ "itself was aimed at being an enjoyable stand-alone experience, not as an overall advertisement for 17 subsequent movies. That mentality has persisted through most of the MCU films over the past decade, which is all the more impressive as its roster of heroes now exceeds the two-dozen mark."[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-THRMarch2018SharedUniverses-343)

#### DC Entertainment, Warner Bros. Pictures, and DC Studios

Main articles: [DC Extended Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DC_Extended_Universe "DC Extended Universe"), [Arrowverse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrowverse "Arrowverse"), and [DC Universe (franchise)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DC_Universe_(franchise) "DC Universe (franchise)")

In October 2012, following its legal victory over [Joe Shuster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Shuster "Joe Shuster")'s estate for the rights to [Superman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superman "Superman"), [Warner Bros. Pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warner_Bros._Pictures "Warner Bros. Pictures") announced that it planned to move ahead with its long-awaited [Justice League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justice_League "Justice League")[film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justice_League_in_other_media#Film "Justice League in other media"), uniting such [DC Comics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DC_Comics "DC Comics") superheroes as [Batman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batman "Batman"), Superman, and [Wonder Woman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wonder_Woman "Wonder Woman"). The company was expected to take the opposite approach to Marvel, releasing individual films for the characters after they have appeared in a [team-up](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Team-up "Team-up") film.[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LATimesOct2012-344) The release of _[Man of Steel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man\_of\_Steel\_(film) "Man of Steel (film)")_ in 2013 was intended to be the start of a new shared universe for DC, "laying the groundwork for the future slate of films based on DC Comics".[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ManofSteel-345) In 2014, Warner Bros. announced that slate of films, similarly to Disney and Marvel claiming dates for films years in advance.[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DCUntitledFilms-346) That year, DC chief creative officer [Geoff Johns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoff_Johns "Geoff Johns") stated that the television series _[Arrow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrow\_(TV\_series) "Arrow (TV series)")_ and _[The Flash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Flash\_(2014\_TV\_series) "The Flash (2014 TV series)")_ were set in a separate universe from the new film one,[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DCSeparateUniverses-347) later clarifying that "We look at it as the [multiverse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiverse "Multiverse"). We have our TV universe and our film universe, but they all co-exist. For us, creatively, it's about allowing everyone to make the best possible product, to tell the best story, to do the best world. Everyone has a vision and you really want to let the visions shine through ... It's just a different approach [from Marvel's]."[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DCMultiverse-348)

Discussing the apparent failure of the cinematic universe's first team-up film, _[Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batman\_v\_Superman:\_Dawn\_of\_Justice "Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice")_ (2016), to establish a successful equivalent to the MCU, Emily St. James noted that where the MCU has a television-like "showrunner" in Feige, "the visionary behind Marvel's entire slate", the DCEU has director [Zack Snyder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zack_Snyder "Zack Snyder"), whose DC films "seemingly start from the assumption that people have come not to see an individual story but a long series of teases for other ones. It's like he knows what he needs to do but can't focus on the task at hand. TV certainly isn't immune to that problem, but shows that get caught up in high-concept premises and big-picture thinking before doing the necessary legwork to establish characters and their relationships tend to be canceled."[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VoxCivilWarTV-318) Subsequently, in May 2016, Warner Bros. gave oversight of the DCEU to Johns and executive Jon Berg in an attempt to "unify the disparate elements of the DC movies" and emulate Marvel's success. The two were made producers on the _Justice League_ films, on top of Johns' involvement in several "solo" films, such as the post-production process of _[Suicide Squad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suicide\_Squad\_(2016\_film) "Suicide Squad (2016 film)")_ (2016) or the writing process of a standalone Batman film.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DCEUShakeUp-349) After the successful release of _[Wonder Woman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wonder\_Woman\_(2017\_film) "Wonder Woman (2017 film)")_ in June 2017, DC decided to begin deemphasizing the shared nature of their films, with DC Entertainment president [Diane Nelson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diane_Nelson_(businesswoman) "Diane Nelson (businesswoman)") stating, "Our intention, certainly, moving forward is using the continuity to help make sure nothing is diverging in a way that doesn't make sense, but there's no insistence upon an overall story line or interconnectivity in that universe... Moving forward, you'll see the DC movie universe being a universe, but one that comes from the heart of the filmmaker who's creating them." Additionally, DC began focusing on films "completely separate from everything else, set entirely outside" the DCEU as part of a new label, with [the first film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joker_(2019_film) "Joker (2019 film)") centered on the [Joker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joker_(character) "Joker (character)").[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VultureDCFilmsSep2017-350) Following the commercial failure of _[Justice League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justice\_League\_(film) "Justice League (film)")_ (2017), which ended the DCEU approach spearheaded by Snyder, Warner Bros. executives reportedly reached out to Feige to have him lead the development of DC films but the talks "fizzled".[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-WSJDCUniverseJul2025-351)

In August 2022, [Warner Bros. Discovery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warner_Bros._Discovery "Warner Bros. Discovery") CEO [David Zaslav](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Zaslav "David Zaslav") announced a 10-year plan for the DC Extended Universe similar to the one that Horn and Iger employed with Feige for the MCU,[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DCEU10YearPlan-352) with James Gunn and [Peter Safran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Safran "Peter Safran") appointed in October 2022 to serve as the co-chairmen and co-CEOs of the newly formed [DC Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DC_Studios "DC Studios") to develop a new shared universe, the [DC Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DC_Universe_(franchise) "DC Universe (franchise)"),[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GunnSafranDCStudios-112) the first content for which was announced in January 2023.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DCStudiosSlate-353) By July 2024, both Feige and Gunn had expressed interest in one day creating a crossover between the two franchises, though both noted it was not something actively being discussed or considered.[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FeigeGunnMarvelDCCrossover2024-354) Gunn revealed following the [second season finale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full_Nelson "Full Nelson") of _[Peacemaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peacemaker\_(TV\_series) "Peacemaker (TV series)")_ in October 2025, that he had wanted to show [Wade Wilson / Deadpool](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wade_Wilson_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Wade Wilson (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") behind one of the alternate universe doors in the [Quantum Unfolding Chamber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pocket_universe "Pocket universe") and had reached out to Deadpool actor [Ryan Reynolds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryan_Reynolds "Ryan Reynolds") about it, who was interested in appearing. However, Gunn noted there would have been "some pretty, pretty big [legal] hoops" to go through to accomplish this, and ultimately moved on from the idea.[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PlannedDeadpoolPeacemakerCameo-355)

#### 20th Century Fox

Main articles: [X-Men (film series)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-Men_(film_series) "X-Men (film series)") and [Fantastic Four in film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantastic_Four_in_film "Fantastic Four in film")

In November 2012, 20th Century Fox announced plans to create its own shared universe of Marvel properties it held the rights to, including the Fantastic Four and X-Men, with the hiring of [Mark Millar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Millar "Mark Millar") as supervising producer. Millar said, "Fox are thinking, 'We're sitting on some really awesome things here. There is another side of the Marvel Universe. Let's try and get some cohesiveness going.' So they brought me in to oversee that really. To meet with the writers and directors to suggest new ways we could take this stuff and new properties that could spin out of it."[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SlashFilmNov2012-356)_[X-Men: Days of Future Past](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-Men:\_Days\_of\_Future\_Past "X-Men: Days of Future Past")_, released in 2014, was Fox's first step towards expanding their stable of Marvel properties and creating this universe,[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IGNFoxSony-357) ahead of the release of a [_Fantastic Four_ reboot film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantastic_Four_(2015_film) "Fantastic Four (2015 film)") the next year.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FantasticFour-358) In May 2014, _Days of Future Past_ and _Fantastic Four_ screenwriter [Simon Kinberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Kinberg "Simon Kinberg") stated that the latter film would not take place in the same universe as the _X-Men_ films, explaining that "none of the _X-Men_ movies have acknowledged the notion of a sort of superhero team—the Fantastic Four. And the Fantastic Four acquire powers, so for them to live in a world where mutants are prevalent is kind of complicated, because you're like, 'Oh, you're just a mutant.' Like, 'What's so fantastic about you?' ... they live in discrete universes."[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FantasticFour-358) In July 2015, _X-Men_ director [Bryan Singer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bryan_Singer "Bryan Singer") said that there was still potential for a crossover between the _X-Men_ and _Fantastic Four_ franchises, if reactions to _Fantastic Four_ and _[X-Men: Apocalypse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-Men:\_Apocalypse "X-Men: Apocalypse")_ (2016) warranted it.[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SingerCrossover-359)

Feeling that Singer's efforts in _Apocalypse_ to establish a larger world, similar to the MCU, did not meet the standards established by Marvel, St. James noted that unlike Feige's ability to serve as "pseudo-showrunner", Singer is instead "steeped in film and the way movie stories have always been told", so "when it comes time to have _Apocalypse_ dovetail with story threads from the earlier _[X-Men: First Class](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-Men:\_First\_Class "X-Men: First Class")_", which was directed by [Matthew Vaughn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthew_Vaughn "Matthew Vaughn"), "both Singer's direction and Simon Kinberg's script rely on hackneyed devices and clumsy storytelling", indicating a lack of "the kind of big-picture thinking this sort of mega franchise requires".[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VoxCivilWarTV-318) In his review of _[Dark Phoenix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dark\_Phoenix\_(film) "Dark Phoenix (film)")_, Joe Morgenstern of _The Wall Street Journal_ characterized the entire X-Men film series as being a "notoriously erratic franchise".[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MorgensternDarkPhoenix-360) In March 2019, the film rights of Deadpool, the X-Men characters, and the Fantastic Four characters returned to Marvel Studios following the [acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney "Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney").[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-FoxDisneyPressRelease-60)[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DisneyFoxDealClose-61)

#### Sony Pictures

Main articles: [Spider-Man in film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man_in_film "Spider-Man in film") and [Sony's Spider-Man Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sony%27s_Spider-Man_Universe "Sony's Spider-Man Universe")

See also: [List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films §Connections with other Spider-Man franchises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films#Connections_with_other_Spider-Man_franchises "List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films")

In November 2013, Sony Pictures Entertainment co-chairman [Amy Pascal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amy_Pascal "Amy Pascal") announced that the studio intended to expand their universe created within director [Marc Webb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marc_Webb "Marc Webb")'s [_The Amazing Spider-Man_ films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(2012_film_series) "The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film series)") (2012–14), with spin-off adventures for supporting characters, in an attempt to replicate Marvel and Disney's model.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IGNFoxSony-357) The next month, Sony announced [Venom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venom_(character) "Venom (character)") and [Sinister Six](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinister_Six "Sinister Six") films, both set in the _Amazing Spider-Man_ universe. With this announcement, _[IGN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IGN "IGN")_ stated that the spin-offs are "the latest example of what we can refer to as "the _Avengers_ effect" in Hollywood, as studios work to build interlocking movie universes."[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VenomSinisterSixIGN-361) Sony chose not to replicate the Marvel Studios model of introducing individual characters first before bringing them together in a team-up film, instead making the Spider-Man adversaries the stars of future films.[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ASM2EW-342) In February 2015, Sony Pictures and Marvel Studios announced that the _Spider-Man_ franchise would be retooled, with a new film co-produced by Feige and Pascal being released in July 2017, and the character being integrated into the MCU. Sony Pictures would continue to finance, distribute, own, and have final creative control of the _Spider-Man_ films.[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SpideyMCU-362) With this announcement, sequels to _[The Amazing Spider-Man 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Amazing\_Spider-Man\_2 "The Amazing Spider-Man 2")_ (2014) were canceled,[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VarietySpidey-363) and by November 2015 the Venom and Sinister Six films, as well as spin-offs based on female characters in the Spider-Man universe, were no longer moving forward.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VarietySpidey-363)[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SpideySpinoffs-364) By March 2016, the Venom film had itself been retooled, to start its own franchise unrelated to the MCU Spider-Man.[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VenomMar2016-365) A year later, Sony officially announced the Venom film to be in development, for an October 5, 2018, release,[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VenomMar2017-366) along with a film centered on the characters [Silver Sable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silver_Sable "Silver Sable") and [Black Cat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Cat_(Marvel_Comics) "Black Cat (Marvel Comics)") known as _[Silver & Black](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silver\_%26\_Black\_(unproduced\_film) "Silver & Black (unproduced film)")_.[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SilverSableBlackCat-367) Both projects were not intended to be a part of the MCU nor spin-offs to _Spider-Man: Homecoming_, but rather part of an intended separate shared universe known as the [Sony's Spider-Man Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sony%27s_Spider-Man_Universe "Sony's Spider-Man Universe") (SSU).[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SilverSableBlackCat-367)[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VenomNotMCU-368)[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-SSU-369) The [mid-credits scene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mid-credits_scene "Mid-credits scene") of _[Venom: Let There Be Carnage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venom:\_Let\_There\_Be\_Carnage "Venom: Let There Be Carnage")_ (2021) hinted at [Eddie Brock / Venom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venom_(Sony%27s_Spider-Man_Universe) "Venom (Sony's Spider-Man Universe)") joining the MCU,[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-LetThereBeCarnagePostCreditsScene-370) which was confirmed with the release of _[Spider-Man: No Way Home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man:\_No\_Way\_Home "Spider-Man: No Way Home")_ (2021) through an uncredited [cameo appearance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cameo_appearance "Cameo appearance") in its mid-credits scene.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-PostCreditsVenom-219)_Spider-Man: No Way Home_ also featured the [Spider-Man iterations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man_in_film "Spider-Man in film") from [Sam Raimi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sam_Raimi "Sam Raimi") and Webb's _Spider-Man_ films, respectively reprised by [Tobey Maguire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tobey_Maguire "Tobey Maguire") and [Andrew Garfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Garfield "Andrew Garfield").[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-MaguireGarfieldSpiderManReprise-371)

After Sony canceled its shared universe plans and began sharing the Spider-Man character with Marvel Studios, multiple critics discussed its failure to replicate the MCU. Scott Meslow of _[The Week](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Week "The Week")_ noted the perceived flaws of the first _Amazing Spider-Man_ film, outside of its lead performances, and how the sequel "doubles down on all the missteps of the original while adding a few of its own. ...We now have a textbook example of how not to reboot a superhero franchise, and if Sony and Marvel are wise, they'll take virtually all those lessons to heart as they chart Spider-Man's next course."[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ASMWeek-372) Scott Mendelson noted that _The Amazing Spider-Man 2_ "was sold as less a sequel to _[The Amazing Spider-Man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Amazing\_Spider-Man\_(2012\_film) "The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film)")_ than a backdoor pilot for _Spider-Man vs. the Sinister Six_. ...Had Sony stuck with the original plan of a scaled-down superhero franchise, one that really was rooted in romantic drama, they would have at least stuck out in a crowded field of superhero franchises. When every superhero film is now going bigger, _Amazing Spider-Man_ could have distinguished itself by going small and intimate." This would have saved Sony "a boatload of money", and potentially reversed the film's relative financial failure.[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ASMForbes-373)

### Academia

In September 2014, the [University of Baltimore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Baltimore "University of Baltimore") announced a course beginning in the 2015 [spring semester](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academic_term "Academic term") revolving around the Marvel Cinematic Universe, to be taught by Arnold T. Blumberg. "Media Genres: Media Marvels" examines "how Marvel's series of interconnected films and television shows, plus related media and comic book sources and [Joseph Campbell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Campbell "Joseph Campbell")'s [monomyth of the 'hero's journey'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monomyth "Monomyth"), offer important insights into modern culture" as well as Marvel's efforts "to establish a viable universe of plotlines, characters, and backstories."[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-UBaltCourse-374)[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-UBaltCourse2-375)

Outside media
-------------

### Avengers Campus

Main article: [Avengers Campus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avengers_Campus "Avengers Campus")

After the acquisition by Disney in 2009, Marvel films began to be marketed at the [Innoventions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Innoventions_(Disneyland) "Innoventions (Disneyland)") attraction in [Tomorrowland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomorrowland_(Disney_Parks) "Tomorrowland (Disney Parks)") at [Disneyland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disneyland "Disneyland"). For _Iron Man 3_, the exhibit, entitled "Iron Man Tech Presented by Stark Industries", featured the same armor display that was shown at the 2012 San Diego Comic-Con, with the Marks I-VII and the new Mark XLII. In addition, there was a simulator game, titled "Become Iron Man", that used [Kinect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinect "Kinect")-like technology to allow the viewer to be encased in an animated Mark XLII armor and take part in a series of "tests", in which you fire repulsor rays and fly through Tony Stark's workshop. The game was guided by J.A.R.V.I.S., who is voiced again by Paul Bettany. The exhibit also had smaller displays that included helmets and chest pieces from the earlier films and the gauntlet and boot from an action sequence in _Iron Man 3_.[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IM3Disneyland-376) The exhibit for _Thor: The Dark World_ was called "Thor: Treasures of Asgard", and featured displays of [Asgardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asgard_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Asgard (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") relics and transports guests to [Odin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odin_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Odin (Marvel Cinematic Universe)")'s throne room, where they were greeted by Thor.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-ThorTDWDisneyland-377)_Captain America: The Winter Soldier_'s exhibit, "Captain America: The Living Legend and Symbol of Courage", featured a meet and greet experience.[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-CapTWSDisneyland-378)

From May to September 2017, Disneyland Resort featured the "Summer of Heroes", which features members of the Guardians and Avengers appearing throughout the Disneyland Resort. Additionally, the Guardians of the Galaxy: Awesome Dance Off event was featured, which involved [Peter Quill / Star-Lord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Quill_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Peter Quill (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") blasting music from his boombox, along with the Avengers Training Initiative, a limited experience where [Black Widow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natasha_Romanoff_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Natasha Romanoff (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") and [Hawkeye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clint_Barton_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Clint Barton (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") "assemble a group of young recruits to see if they have what it takes to be an Avenger." Marvel-related food and merchandise was also available throughout [Hollywood Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood_Land "Hollywood Land") at [Disney California Adventure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disney_California_Adventure "Disney California Adventure") during the "Summer of Heroes".[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GotGBreakoutOpening-379)

In March 2018, the Walt Disney Company announced three new Marvel-themed areas inspired by the MCU to Disney California Adventure, [Walt Disney Studios Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Paris "Walt Disney Studios Paris"), and [Hong Kong Disneyland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong_Disneyland "Hong Kong Disneyland"). The developments were designed by [Walt Disney Imagineering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Disney_Imagineering "Walt Disney Imagineering") in collaboration with Marvel Studios and Marvel Themed Entertainment.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VarietyDisneyParks-380) As was established with [_Guardians of the Galaxy_ – Mission: Breakout!](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardians_of_the_Galaxy_%E2%80%93_Mission:_Breakout! "Guardians of the Galaxy – Mission: Breakout!"), Avengers Campus exists in its own theme park universe that is inspired by the MCU.[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GotGBreakoutMCUConnection-381)[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AvengersCampusMultiverse-382) Being in the MCU multiverse, Avengers Campus has a shared history with the MCU proper, with a few notable exceptions being [the Blip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Blip "The Blip") from _Avengers: Infinity War_ did not occur, and some characters who died, such as Tony Stark, are still alive.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AvengersCampusMultiverse-382)

#### Hong Kong Disneyland

In October 2013, the [Iron Man Experience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Man_Experience "Iron Man Experience") attraction was announced for Hong Kong Disneyland.[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IronManExperience-383) It is set in the [Tomorrowland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomorrowland_(Disney_Parks) "Tomorrowland (Disney Parks)") section of the park,[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IMExpDS-384) with the area built to look like a new Stark Expo created by Tony Stark after the 2010 one, as seen in _Iron Man 2_,[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IMExpStarkExpo-385) with various exhibit halls that include the Mark III armor from the films.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IMExpDS-384)[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IMExpMKIII-386) The area also has Iron Man and Marvel-themed merchandise items and memorabilia, plus an interactive game where guests can have the chance to try on Iron Man's armor.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IMExpReleaseDate-387) Iron Man Experience sees guests assist Iron Man in defeating Hydra throughout Hong Kong,[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IMExpDS-384) and opened on January 11, 2017.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-IMExpReleaseDate-387)

In March 2018, the Walt Disney Company announced a new Marvel-themed area inspired by the MCU to Hong Kong Disneyland and a new attraction where guests team up with Ant-Man and the Wasp, to join Iron Man Experience.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-VarietyDisneyParks-380)[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-DisneyParksMar2018-388) Inspired by _Ant-Man and the Wasp_,[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AMWaspRide-389)[Ant-Man and The Wasp: Nano Battle!](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant-Man_and_The_Wasp:_Nano_Battle! "Ant-Man and The Wasp: Nano Battle!") is an enclosed interactive dark ride that sees guests use laser-powered weapons to team up with Ant-Man and the Wasp to defeat [Arnim Zola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arnim_Zola_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Arnim Zola (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") and his army of Hydra swarm bots.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AMWaspRide-389)[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AMWaspRideName-390) Ant Man and the Wasp: Nano Battle! replaces the [Buzz Lightyear Astro Blasters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzz_Lightyear_attractions "Buzz Lightyear attractions") ride,[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AMWaspRide-389) and opened on March 31, 2019.[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-AMWaspRideOpen-391)

#### Disney California Adventure

By San Diego Comic-Con 2016, the [Tower of Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Twilight_Zone_Tower_of_Terror "The Twilight Zone Tower of Terror") at Disney California Adventure was set to be replaced by a new attraction, _Guardians of the Galaxy_ – Mission: Breakout!. [Chris Pratt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Pratt "Chris Pratt"), [Zoë Saldaña](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zo%C3%AB_Salda%C3%B1a "Zoë Saldaña"), [Dave Bautista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Bautista "Dave Bautista") and [Benicio del Toro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benicio_del_Toro "Benicio del Toro") all filmed exclusive footage for the attraction, reprising their roles as [Peter Quill / Star-Lord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Quill_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Peter Quill (Marvel Cinematic Universe)"), [Gamora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamora_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Gamora (Marvel Cinematic Universe)"), [Drax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drax_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Drax (Marvel Cinematic Universe)") and [Taneleer Tivan / The Collector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collector_(Marvel_Cinematic_Universe) "Collector (Marvel Cinematic Universe)"), respectively.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GotGBreakout-392)[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GotGBreakout2-393) James Gunn, director of _Guardians of the Galaxy_ and its sequel, directed footage for the attraction and consulted on all aspects of it.[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GotGBreakoutGunn-394)_Guardians of the Galaxy_ – Mission: Breakout! sees visitors assisting Rocket in rescuing the other Guardians from the Collector's fortress, while the attraction features randomized events throughout the experience and music inspired by the _[Awesome Mix Vol. 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardians\_of\_the\_Galaxy:\_Awesome\_Mix\_Vol.\_1\_(Original\_Motion\_Picture\_Soundtrack) "Guardians of the Galaxy: Awesome Mix Vol. 1 (Original Motion Picture Soundtrack)")_ soundtrack. The attraction opened on May 27, 2017.[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe#cite_note-GotGBreakoutOpening-379)

In March 2018, the Walt Disney Company announced a new Marvel-themed area inspired by the MCU at Disney California Adventure, anchored by Mission: Breakout!, that features characters from the MCU, such as Iron Man and Spider-Man, joining the Guardians of the Galaxy in a "completely immersive superhero universe".
